# The Creative Process Behind Big Ideas

A bit of an advanced / high level post for today — I hope this gives you all some ideas and direction :)

Have you ever seen brands like Naval, Mark Manson, Jack Butcher and others just to be consumed by the depth behind their ever-so-simple ideas?

The ideas that make you stop and think, "Damn, I wish I wrote that..."

The ideas that stick in your head for eternity — making you market their brand through word of mouth?

This is also why some books do better than others. Why you have your favorite books that you always recommend to your friends.

It isn't the quality of their writing, it is the quality of their ideas.

The best one-liner tweets are big ideas — but few have actual depth behind them. This is the next step in building a highly authoritative brand. Not just generating good ideas, but developing good ideas into big ideas.

You may have noticed that my newsletters, ideas, and depth/articulation of concepts on the podcast have had a considerable jump in quality. This is due to my creative workflow. Moreso, this is due to me working LESS. I will break it all down here.

Idea Generation

We've talked about this many times. You generate good ideas by consuming good content and noting down what sticks out to you.

Books, podcasts, Twitter threads, articles, audiobooks, and content from those you aspire to be like.

Time must be scheduled for consumption. Instead of thinking of it as consumption — think of it as research.

Content creation is 80% research, 20% creating content. (GOOD content, that is).

The ideas that spark excitement — dopamine — as you are "researching" are the things you should put in your notes. You must get in the habit of writing everything down that sticks out to you.

You must also schedule time for nothingness or no thought. Meditative activities that have the potential of pushing you into a flow state. Self-competition.

Martial arts. The gym. Meditation. Disc golf (been playing this a lot recently). Yoga. Running. Swimming. Sunbathing. Long walks. Nature bathing. Hiking. Etc.

This is more important than you think. "Idea generation" time — or active recovery — takes up much more time in my day than actual focused work does.

Start replacing those negative habits with some of these meditative activities.

While you are doing these activities, better ideas will pop into your head (thank you subconscious mind\!)

Take note of these immediately when they come to mind.

I have a running note in my phone that I call "The Queue" for all of my research notes and ideas that pop into my head as I'm going about my day.

Idea Development

Consumption \= good ideas.

Active recovery \= better ideas.

Now we must develop these into BIG ideas. The ideas that we will be known for. Here's how I do it.

I have scheduled time in my day to go through The Queue.

I personally use Roam Research, but you can use whatever note-taking software you want. Obsidian, Evernote, or Notion are probably your best bet.

There are 2 types of note-taking that I would recommend reading up on. Smart Notes and the Zettelkasten Method.

Personally, I would treat these as training wheels. Over time you will develop your own way of writing, deciphering, and turning your notes into big ideas.

Here is how I have been doing it:

 All of my notes, insights, and ideas are inside The Queue (random notes that have stacked up throughout the week)  
I scroll through and pick something that interests me, or just start going down and organizing them  
I expand on that note with my personal insights and summary of the idea  
Personal insights are experiences I've had with that idea and WHY it is so relevant to my life. The summary is just me expanding on it to get more ideas flowing  
After I have 2-3 paragraphs of information — I read through it and summarize the entire thing as a one-sentence BIG idea  
Then, I add in links to other relevant notes or big ideas and start to go back through The Queue  
I can start the process over again or find things that relate to that big idea to develop it further.

Now, when its time to create content, you have an incredible concept with a lot of depth behind it.

This is how you create a weeks worth of content without trying. Some call this their "second brain" or similar.

What can you do with these big ideas?

Use them as content inspiration or just let them stack up.

I personally write a banger newsletter, write tweets along the way, use the newsletter as a YouTube script, and have those newsletters saved for later when I want to start releasing blog content

Simple Frameworks & Systems

To take this even further, start to combine your big ideas or turn them into frameworks / systems that you can call your own.

"Personal Monopoly" is a big idea from Jack Butcher — the HOW behind this big idea is his framework or system. Now, I haven't taken his course, but I am sure this concept is brought up and broken down in a simple, step-by-step process.

One of my big ideas from the other day was "You can turn negative thoughts, feelings, and emotions into a positive potential outcome in life."

As I was writing out my summary (what) and personal experiences (why), I began formulating a framework (how).

I called it the Conscious Conditioning Process.

I have a newsletter coming out this Friday about it.

I can talk about this process whenever I am asked about "how to deal with negative thoughts and emotions."

I am writing about this in my book.

Hell, I could even create a product on this alone. (People buy systems that get results.)

People will start to attribute this process to me, word will spread, and my brand will indirectly grow because of it.

The frameworks/systems you create, name, and tie to yourself are what you will be remembered for. People will pass these along.

Why? Behavior change.

This is the only thing that matters. "What's" and "why's" are good for content, they grab attention. But people want to implement the "how."

The "what" gets them interested, the "how" gets them results (that they attribute to you), the "why" gets them to take action (because it is emotion based).

If your framework gets them results, they will tell a friend about it. Your name will spread and you will start getting tagged on social media when other people are talking about similar topics.

Creating These In A Productive Way

You should have a product / project you are working on that you can tie all of these ideas back to.

Since this research, nothingness, and idea development time is worked into my days — my current book, future book, and future products are creating themselves.

I let my curiosity guide me to learn and implement new things. Then I just turn them into content quickly.

---

# The Risk Reversal \- Your Secret Weapon For More Clients & Sales

Landing your first client, increasing your conversion rate, selling more products, and creating a compelling offer is difficult... so I'm going to make it a lot easier on you.

When it comes to selling anything (freelance services, coaching, consulting, digital products, physical products)... specificity matters.

Especially when it comes to your promised result (the things that potential customers care about most. We discussed the Quantifiable End Result inside Your Marketing Strategy In One Sentence.

I will bring you 5 new qualified leads this week \> I will do lead generation for you.  
You will lose 10 pounds per month \> You will lose weight

Any promise you give should be as specific as you can make it. 

This gives the potential customer something quantifiable. Something they can make sense of. It sparks desire.

(Pair this with a unique system to get those results and ding ding you have a semi-incredible offer)

This creates a problem for beginners.

They don't have any results to back these numbers up. It's hard for you to display your value to clients.

There is the traditional "permissionless apprenticeship" approach where you send free work, let them test it out, then start working for them (or get a testimonial in return).

This works, but we can add more firepower to start getting paid. More risk reversal.

If you are confident in the product or service that you offer \- throw a number out there. What do results do you think you can get them?

Let's say for a social media growth service \- 2,000 followers a month minimum.  
How about an email marketing service for coaches \- 5 sales calls booked.  
Fitness coaching? 10 pounds lost in the first month.  
Performance coaching? Reducing the amount of time you work by 2 hours.

Now we are working with something. You should be confident in the numbers that you are throwing out.

If you aren't skilled enough to do this, get better at what you do. Help people for free. Understand their business / life. Dig into their problems and give them the solutions.

Systemize it.

Make it easy to get them results.

But... what happens if you don't get them that result? That's where the risk reversal comes in. Usually in the form of a refund (because they are paying for the result with money, that's the risk).

You can get creative with this. You can offer to work with them a second month for free, work with them until they do get those results, or offer some form of that is worth something. (These work great for coaches).

For social media \- If I don't bring you 2,000 followers this month, you won't pay a cent. (You can even go as far to say that you will pay them an extra $100 on top just for wasting their time... who can refuse that?)  
For email marketing \- If I don't bring you 5 new calendar books this month, I will refund you the cost of service.  
For fitness coaching \- If you don't lose 10 pounds this month, I will work with you until you lose 15 pounds for free.

Not only does this make your offer irresistible, it acts as accountability and gives you real-world experience.

If you don't get results, you don't get paid. So you better get results.  
Now... you will have to set criteria for some of these.

You can't just promise someone to lose 10 pounds, they end up doing nothing to actually get there, and you have to refund them because you didn't set boundaries.

Same goes for email marketing. If they have a dead email list filled with people that are not interested in coaching... it's going to be near impossible to get calendar bookings.

This is why qualification and setting hard criteria works. It holds you AND the client accountable.

You can get creative with all of this and use it for digital products as well. (You will just have to set harder criteria... which is good because it will encourage people to actually use the product).

Simple, no?

Get specific. Add a risk reversal. Make it the forefront of your marketing.

---

# A Breakdown Of My Previous Twitter Agency

Here is exactly what I did to close 4 clients in 2 weeks at $3500/month a piece.

For those that don't know (and I don't expect many to know), I created a Twitter management / growth agency a while back. It ended up falling apart because my previous partner and I had different interests, we decided to just abandon the idea altogether after 2 months.

The Offer

Here are the components of our offer:

4 tweets a day  
1 thread a week  
$750 monthly budget for paid RTs (guaranteed growth)  
DM management  
Engage with people in the replies

Our guarantee: we make them their money back or we refund them what the difference (if they made $2500, we refund $1000)

Our target market: personal brands with top selling courses (makes it easy to make their money back)

Our USP: My partner and I are both great tweet writers, the people we reached out to can see that. We have "celebrity" credibility.  
How We Delivered

First, we understood how to grow twitter accounts and make sales because we had already done it ourselves.

(Remember that learning how to deliver your service is extremely important. This shouldn't have to be said but it seems like too many people want everything give to them, like in this post, and just expect it to work.)

In reality people have already done this work for you. Its called a Twitter course. You can take a twitter course, systemize it, and turn it into the backbone of your account management offer. This is also how you learn how to grow on Twitter.

Other skills that are required:  
Understanding of personal brands sales process  
Light understanding of copywriting for promotional content  
Proficiency in writing, specifically short form content (tweets) and blog style content (threads)

How we came up with content ideas:  
We got access to their courses and turned it into authority content  
We studied competitors in their niche on Instagram and YouTube and use it as content inspiration  
We had the client fill out an extensive questionnaire asking for their content pillars, topics, tone of voice, likes, dislikes, accomplishments, etc  
We created a swipe file from their top tweets in analytics and reword a lot of them

We would send them a weeks worth of tweets to refine and approve. This would help us understand their voice better over time. We would do the same with threads.

We would schedule the tweets in Hypefury and plug their course once a day under a tweet that we knew would do well and was relevant to their course.  
How We Landed Clients

We closed 80% of the people we reached out to because our offer is very specific, has a great guarantee, and we targeted people that we know had money (top selling course creators).

You can find these by searching for the best sellers on gumroad, or finding coaches / creators that you vibe with on Instagram or YouTube and offer to increase their course sales and build their authority on Twitter.

We followed this outreach method to a T and used a personal video. We recorded ourselves going over the outreach message and talked like normal human beings.

All clients except one closed without a sales call because our offer was that good.  
How Can You Do This?

Study as much Twitter content / courses as possible (like this one with JK Molina or this one with Eddy Quan)  
Practice by growing an account of your own, preferably in the niche / interest area that you would enjoy writing about and has profitable creators in  
Systemize your process for content creation, sales, engagement, and replies  
Write content for others or get on a call with them to give them strategies to get more out of their account  
If you aren't extremely confident in your ability, start out at a low cost and increase it as you get results / testimonials  
Create smaller offers (like $500 for 20 tweets and a thread)

One last thing to note:

Stop trying to make money extremely quickly. All it will do is burn you out. Take your time, have fun with the process, and GET GOOD at what you do.

I know many of you are wanting to start a twitter agency so I hope this helped.

---

# The Hero Section \- Sales Page Copywriting Part 1

Whats good my friends, over the next few weeks I'm going to break down my personal copywriting framework that has gotten some killer results over the past year or so.

As a prerequisite \- you will need to understand the concepts from these articles:

Your Entire Marketing Strategy In One Sentence (your target, unique mechanism, quantifiable end result) this will be your main focus, but you must understand the articles below as well  
Narrowing Further and The Start of Market Research (understanding your target)  
Market Sophistication, Customer Awareness, and Research (understanding the deep problems and objections of your target)  
Standing Out From The Competition (Your USP)

As you can probably tell... these articles might be making more sense now. They are the foundation of an effective marketing strategy for your offers.

The articles above help you craft an irresistible offer and write irresistible copy. 

The Hero Section

The "hero section" is what everyone sees when they first land on your sales page.

Also \- a sales page is going to be a bit different from a full website. Just keep that in mind. This is for your products/services that you want to sell on a single, high-performing page.

Your job is to unleash MOST of your marketing firepower here.

Your USP  
Your unique mechanism (optional but should be hinted at)  
Your quantifiable end result (what people want for their transformation)  
Your target audience (so they know the message is for them)  
Their deepest, most bothersome problem (start of the transformation)  
Your risk reversal (optional but can be hinted at)

The hero section is EASILY the most important part of your sales page. This is where people will decide if they keep reading.

The Eyebrow

![][image1]

The eyebrow is an option section that goes at the very top of the page \- above the headline.

I use it to:

Call out my target audience (creators, coaches, freelancers, experts, etc.)  
Call out the main problem they are experiencing (consistent monetization)

This will give the reader a little spurt of dopamine and make them thing "hey this is written for me\!"

The Headline

IMPORTANT AS F\*CK

Writing headlines is an art. They grab attention and are the main thing that people read.

I personally use it for:

My USP  
The quantifiable end result  
Getting to that quantifiable end result without X inconvenience  
If you can use numbers, even better

Examples:

Discover How A 24 Year Old Turned A Non Original Business Idea Into $12,500 In Just 3 Days  
Discover The Only Platform You Need To Master Your Mind, Body, and Spirit While Growing a $5,000 \- $10,000 per Month Online Business  
Steal The Proven Strategies, Processes, and Systems That Fuel Multi-Six Figure Social Media Businesses & Cut Your Work Times In Half

The secret to this is piecing together certain parts of your marketing material here.

How can they all fit cohesively in the hero section?

How do they make the most sense in your eyebrow, headline, and deck?

The Deck

Your deck (some people call it a subheadline) gives people a taste about what to expect when they continue reading \- it's supposed to build desire and make them WANT to continue reading.

This is where you try to fit the marketing firepower that you haven't already used in your headline or eyebrow.

Most of the time, I pop part of my USP into it and make it sound juicy and use it to tell them what they will receive if they continue reading.

If you didn't have room for eliminating an inconvenience, add it to the deck.

You can also hint at your unique mechanism here.

Examples:

Get immediate access to the Twitter Lead System and stop worrying about where your next client will come from  
Get step-by-step guidance from a marketing & performance consultant to seamlessly build a $10K+ per month online business (without having to buy another program... for life)

If you have any questions, pop them in the respective Lounge channel.

Start rewriting those eyebrows, headlines, and decks my friends\!

---

# The Body \- Sales Page Copywriting Part 2 (and intro to PASTOR)

In last weeks article we discussed the The Hero Section of a sales page which includes (or hints at) most of our marketing firepower.

The eyebrow, headline, and deck.

Now \- we have people attention. They know that the page is speaking to them, and they are curious to see how you can solve their problem.

Keep in mind, we are talking about the framework in these articles, not the writing itself. We will talk about that later, but the framework alone can make up for some writing skills.

Initial Social Proof

This part is optional, but after talking with a few freelance copywriters, they swear by this to hold attention from the start.

This part is simple, introduce some of your top case studies / testimonials with a brief explanation of the results they got.

Here is my example from the MMHQ landing page.

This comes right after the deck (or VSL, a video sales letter if you have one)

Squash peoples disbelief early with results you've gotten and build the desire even more.

Introducing The PASTOR Framework

You've probably heard of AIDA (attention, interest, desire, action)... but that is basic and lacks nuance.

It's good, don't get me wrong, but PASTOR does it better (and provides a better formula for longer form content).

Here is an article that goes more in depth.

P \- problem  
A \- amplify  
S \- story \+ solution  
T \- transformation \+ testimony  
O \- Offer  
R \- Response (CTA)

I use this for nearly ALL of my writing, not just sales pages.

Blogs, threads, emails, etc.

The Lead

By far one of the most important parts of your copy aside from the hero section.

Everytime I read good copy, if the lead is very good, I am ready to buy right then in there.

The lead is an accurate description of the problem(s) they are facing right now that you can solve. This is where MUCH of your market research comes into play.

If you can NAIL the readers specific situation, they will be open to hearing what you have to say, if not buy right there.

Your lead should paint a picture of the pressing problem (this is also the P in the PASTOR framework).

You can format your copy however you'd like \- but bullet points that state their current painful situation in detail are always a good move.

You are talking directly to them, making them understand that the position they are in isn't a good one.

You can also include the "A" of PASTOR here, Amplify the problem. Make them understand why they need a change.

Throughout all of this you are both taking into account the market's level of sophistication AND their level of awareness.

If you are promoting a self-improvement product to an incredibly saturated market \- nailing the problem they are having is crucial, because they have probably already tried many self-help books and YouTube tutorials/blogs.

They are more than likely aware of their problem, you just need to jab at it and amplify it.

You can get as creative as you want with how you introduce these bullet points.

On the MMHQ landing page, I labeled them as "traps" that creators, coaches, or freelancers fall into.

Here is how I introduced the lead:

Here are the bullet point problems:

The key to this is getting VERY specific. This is very easy if your target audience is your former self.

Next up \- the body.

The Body

At the start of the body you should have another headline that brings attention to the solution of their problem.

The body is where you start to build a story on how the previous problem was solved. How somebody had this problem and eventually solved it via your product or service.

(This is the first part of "S" in PASTOR, the story. The solution is where you introduce your offer)

Humans love stories. It keeps them hooked and reading if you can write it well.

Beginning \- how the protagonist had the problem you described (paint their life and what it looked like, emphasize reliability, talk about what their actual lifestyle looked like).

Middle \- The turning point and introduction of your unique mechanism.

End \- Their results, we will introduce your offer soon as the solution.

If you do not think you have a story to tell \- you are either lying to yourself or you need to create one.

You can tell:

Your own personal story (works well if you don't have social proof)  
A client success story (hence why I think having consultations beforehand is important)

The story doesn't even need to be a story about a person. You can simply walk them through a hypothetical of where they are now and how they can get to the solution.

Use "what ifs." \- these aren't as powerful, but they are a story nonetheless.

In the story (all of your copy actually), you should take into account the objections the reader has. These should be written down already. Explain how those objections mean nothing by bringing them up and turning them into selling points.

When you are writing your story \- think of how you can word things in a way that will "click" with the reader.

Here is the intro to my body from the MMHQ landing page:

Joey's story fit the strategy to perfection \- especially since he is now a partner of MMHQ. Who wouldn't want to learn from the purple man himself after that transformation?\!

That's about it for this article.

In the next one we will talk about your unique mechanism, offer introduction, call to action, and other parts that will round out your sales page.

If you have any questions, pop em in respective Lounge channels\!

---

# The Godfather Offer \- A Plug & Play Template

I'm going to make him an offer he can't refuse...

Prerequisites for this post:

What You Need To Understand For Your Social Media Business  
The First Thing To Do When Starting an Online Business  
Narrowing Further & Market Research  
Market Sophistication and Customer Awareness  
Your Entire Marketing Strategy In One Sentence

In short: what product/service can you create that aligns with everything we’ve talked about previously?

What fits this strategy to perfection?

What can you create that actually delivers the quantifiable end result for your target?

This is where everything comes together.

Your offer is an exchange of value.

How can you present your offer in a way that is OVERWHELMINGLY valuable in exchange for the asking price?

It’s time to start thinking of your offer in more ways than just a product or service. There is much much more that comes into play here.

Components of an Irresistible Offer

It’s time to start thinking of your offer in more ways than just a product or service. There is much much more that comes into play here.

1\. Pricing

Value based pricing

How do people charge thousands of dollars for a few videos (in a course)? They provide an overwhelming amount of value for the price.

If you can nearly guarantee someone results \- and their PROBLEM is BIG enough, they will pay the price to have your solution.

When crafting the rest of your offer, take competitor prices into account.  
Are you providing more than they are?

Can you offer a lower (but respectable) price?

We also discussed pricing a bit more in this post.

2\. Bonuses

Bonuses can be used in multiple ways \- the main thing is… you need to be able to offer bonuses.

For price negotiation (not directly included in the offer):

If somebody says the price is “too high” or they do not have enough \- do not lower your price. It decreases the value of your offer.

Instead, offer them a relevant bonus (that is not included in the offer) to push them over the edge and get them to buy.

Example: $1500 is too much for a website \- offer them a free landing page valued at $500 to push them over the edge

Included in your offer:

What bonuses, relevant to your main product or service, can you bake into the offer to add higher perceived value?

Let’s say my main product is a web design course… I can offer bonuses like:

An SEO guide so people can get more organic traffic to their site  
A free 30 minute coaching session to help them make use of it  
A Slack or Discord community where buyers can interact  
A website checklist to make it easy for them to create websites

Bonuses will justify your pricing and result in an extremely happy customer.  
Some people buy products solely for the bonus items.

3\. Risk Reversal (Social Proof Included)

What will make the reader understand that there is ABSOLUTELY ZERO RISK from buying from you?

This comes down to a few things.

Payment options (split payments, financing, etc)  
Money back guarantee  
Social proof  
Other proof that shows your offer WORKS  
Guaranteeing QER or else you receive X bonus

We will discuss the Negative Risk concept one of these days in an article format.

4\. Discounts

Discounts should be used sparingly (depending on the platform or method)

Discounts for holidays, special events, and milestones are a good idea \- not much to touch on there.

One thing to take into account is CONTRAST.

You should talk about the true value of your offer compared to the price you are offering it at.

“Coaches charge $2500 for 3 months of hand holding. I am giving you all of the information you need for $47.”

“Realistically, this website would go for $10,000 when designed by a big agency, I am giving you it today for $5000.”

“Everything included in this bundle is worth $449, you get it for $25”  
You get the point.

Use this to your advantage when selling both verbally and written.

Offer Stacking

Offer stacking is an INCREDIBLE way to sell more of your service.

Side note: if you can create a course, you can create a service. You SHOULD create a service.. Whether it's freelancing, coaching, consulting, or all of the above.

Example of An Offer Stack

I am now a freelancer. I charge e-commerce stores $5000/month to implement the Email Domination funnel (random name off the top of my head).

When I am on a sales call with the decision maker of this e-commerce store, they may have objections about the price, OR just not be able to afford it.

SO, I now have a backup offer. I can implement a piece of the Email Domination Funnel for half the price ($5000 one time fee). Rather than the entire funnel, I write specific sequences and hand them off to the store.  
If this is still too much, I can offer consulting for $2500. 8 calls and I teach them how to implement the entire Email Domination Funnel by themselves.  
   
They get all of the value of the $5000/month service at a fraction of the cost.

At this point, $2500 one time fee seems like NOTHING compared to $5000/month.

Example For Coaches

First offer: The Actualization Program ($5000)

Full fledged 3 month program.

Second offer: The Accelerated Program ($2500)

Accelerated 1.5 month program. Same value \+ material, half the time and half the calls (still extremely appealing).

Third offer: The Micro Program ($500)

2 weeks of DM or Telegram access, no calls. You assign them content from the program and talk them through it.

Now, once they go through any of these programs, you can upsell them on a micro coaching monthly retainer. $500/month with little time investment on your end. Let your mind run wild and get creative with this.

As with everything in marketing... this will get better with time, experience, and iteration. Don't get discouraged if you don't get this right the first time.

---

# Your Entire Marketing Strategy In One Sentence

To make things extremely simple, we are going to turn your entire marketing strategy into a one-sentence description.

This will help you regain clarity when you fall off track.

I learned about this sentence from Dan Henry, but before we dive into what it actually is, we need other parts of our marketing locked down.

Your Ideal Customer

Your ideal customer is the person you would thoroughly enjoy working with. They have more than enough funds to afford your service without being needy or annoying. They "vibe" with you and understand that you are the expert.

You determine your ideal customer through marketing research and reverse engineering a starving market.

This article will help you reverse engineer the market.

This article will help you paint your ideal customer.

Your Unique System

We haven't talked about this much yet \- but your unique system is YOUR method / path / way for getting results.

Remember P90X? Their unique system was "muscle confusion," a completely BS term that spread across the world. (Do this ethically, don't just make shit up like them)

My unique system for social media creators is the Social Matrix.

Many people can show you how to build out a funnel \- but very few people have a system specific to social media that brings an insane amount of traffic (without ad costs).

Whenever you see people promoting a specific method that gets results, that is their unique system.

Somebody that does Facebook Ads for local businesses can have the "local celebrity funnel" which is just a series of ads and landing pages that is spun in a unique way.

That's the thing about this \- it may not necessarily be unique \- but it isn't a generic solution to a burning problem. It isn't a commodity.

One last example for web designers, what is more enticing:

A website that captures more leads  
The Appointment Accelerator (a landing page, lead magnet, and email followups to book appointments for service businesses)

Your Quantifiable End Result (OR Promise)

Think about the transformation that you offer your customers/clients. (That's what marketing / sales is, giving people a solution to a problem \- causing some degree of transformation in their life).

Point A \= where they are now

Point B \= where your product / service can take them (where your unique system will take them.)

Point B is your promise. It is OK if you can't make it absolutely quantifiable.

We want to spice up point B a bit more by making it quantifiable.

When you are thinking about hiring a fitness coach, what is more enticing?

Losing weight for the summer  
Losing 25 pounds in 3 months

Clearly number 2\.

The potential client / customer can visualize number 2\. It's tangible.

Number 1 means they can lose 5 pounds or 50 pounds, it's not specific. Specificity is always better in marketing.

When you're providing a marketing service for a company, what is more enticing?

I will send you qualified leads each month  
I will send you 10 qualified leads per month or I will refund your investment and pay you $100 on top.

Number 2 wins yet again.

Be specific with the outcome that your offer provides.

(This becomes 10x more powerful when you can back it up with social proof and testimonials.)

Your Entire Marketing Strategy In One Sentence

From Dan Henry:

If I can make \[ideal customer\] believe that \[unique system\] is the only way to get \[quantifiable end result\] and the only way to do that is through \[my offer\], then all objections become irrelevant, and they must invest.

Let's plug in an example.

Ideal customer \= creators (that are hovering around $2-$3k/month)

Unique mechanism \= the social matrix and infinity funnel

Quantifiable end result \= $1 per follower per month

Offer \= The Brand Mastery Program

Here is my marketing strategy in one sentence:

If I can make creators believe that the social matrix and infinity funnel is the only way to make $1 per follower per month, and the only way to do that is through the Brand Mastery Program, then all objections become irrelevant, and they must invest.

Once you have this down, it really is all up to your offer.

---

# Why Your Copy, Promotions, & Sales Calls Suffer

We all know that selling is an emotional game. You have to toy with your potential customer's heartstrings (and for good reason, your product will help them avoid that feeling again).

Negative emotions sell more than positive. Both are useful, but we are providing solutions to a problem that creates those negative emotions.

The more specific you get, the better.

Like telling a story, you want to paint a picture of where their life is now (negative impact of the problem) and where their life will be (solution).

A great way to do this is by breaking it down and understanding the biological root of the problem.

Quite frankly, the potential customer thinks they have a certain problem \- when in reality it is something else.

Here's what you should do.

Step 1: List Out Your Target’s Main Problems

Refer back to what you wrote down for your market research in this previous post.

Take note of what they are struggling with the most and normal pain points within that niche.

Order them from most pressing to least pressing. Which causes them the most emotional pain?

All of these pain points will play a role in our marketing, but the main problem is the most important, and helps you understand your customer more.

Step 2: Discover The Biological Root

Emotions \> Logic

Especially in marketing. People buy results. Results stem from greed and necessity.

Now, we are going to break down the \#1 problem from above and break it down even further (people who are familiar with sales understand the power of this.)

Let’s pretend we are on a sales call here \- I am pitching a Twitter follower on high-performance coaching (self-improvement/productivity stuff).

I get on the call, let him know how it is going to go, ask some questions, and get to this part of the call:

Tell me man, what are you struggling the most with right now? Whats preventing you from reaching X result?"

“Well, it seems like I’ve lost focus during my work and I have a LOT to get done. It is stressing me out.”

In your daily life, what is this costing you? Why does it matter that this work isn’t getting done?

“I’m not able to give the time and energy to my wife and kids at night. I don’t see an end to the work I’m doing.”

(We are getting somewhere here).

What do you think is causing this to happen right now?

“Answers the question”

Is this affecting other people in your life, how?

“Yes, my wife is getting tired of me, my kids are upset, and I haven’t seen my friends in months.”

(Ending up alone is a biological problem/fear.)

What will happen if you don’t solve this problem in 90 ish days?

“I may never talk to my friends again… and who knows, my wife could consider leaving me”

See what we did here? We broke down a surface-level problem of a lack of focus and turned it into something much much deeper, and much more pressing.

What you need to do, is take your \#1 ranked problem and ask questions about it until you get to the root.

Your job is to make them realize what the biological root of the problem is. 99% percent of the time you don't explicitly say it.

Then, you can transition into pitching your solution.

---

# Offer Creation Part 1 \- Pricing

Let's talk about pricing your offers, both low ticket and high ticket.

Low ticket \= $1000 or less.  
High ticket \= $1000+

Some people consider high ticket $5000+ but for the sake of understanding this, let's stick to \+/- $1000.

The Problem \- Time and Market-Based Pricing

Many freelancers and coaches make the mistake of going with time-based pricing from the start. This almost always causes headaches that you will change down the road... so it's better to just start charging in a better way now.

Info products that are based on the market value of other products also pigeon holes you.

Your pricing should be solely dependent on the return your are bringing the other person \- you need to be able to articulate that value (we will discuss tactics for this later.)

The Solution \- Value-Based Pricing

How do people charge thousands of dollars for a few videos (in a course)? They provide an overwhelming amount of value for the price.

How do people charge $50k for high-level coaching? They solve a $100k problem. The value exceeds the payment

If you can nearly guarantee someone results \- and their PROBLEM is BIG enough, they will pay the price to have your solution.

Many problems within the health/wealth/relationships verticals are big enough to charge big prices. This is why it is very important to follow the steps we've talked about earlier with the customer avatar, market research, unique positioning, etc.

When determining your pricing, take competitor prices into account (but not to match their price, unless it is an extremely similar offer).

Are you providing more than they are?

My twitter/marketing/funnel consulting all in one is much more valuable than a generic online business program \- because it solves a specific (and very pressing) problem and gets a specific type of person results.

What unique strengths do you have that can make your solution more effective? (Think about your USP)

For me \- its twitter. I have leverage and more knowledge than the average person in that area. The main part of my offer is marketing/funnels \- but I can help others drive insane traffic to theirs via Twitter as opposed to ads or other methods.

Can you offer a lower (but respectable) price?

Proceed with caution on lowering your prices as it will attract people looking for a 'deal.'

I would say that this is only useful if your offer is very productized and doesn't take up too much of your time.

Take the SCAMPER method into account.

Read up on the method here.

This takes some creativity, time, and subconscious processing to do right \- don't try to lock this down all in one go.

In short, what parts of your offer can you substitute, combine, adapt, modify, put to other use, eliminate, or reverse to make your offer more enticing?

In future posts, we will discuss other parts of your offer and how everything we've talked about fits together.

If you have any questions so far post it in \#Business Strategy\!

---

# Offer Stacking For More Sales & Negotiation

What I mean by offer stack is having different tiers/options for your high ticket offer.

Freelance, consulting, or coaching service.

If you don't have a service yet, you should.

Services should come before products because it is easier to iterate and get results. (There is nuance to this. It is dependent on your goals).

By iterating, you are creating your own unique method for getting results (this is important). Your unique system.

THEN, you can package your unique system up into a product and leverage the results / testimonials it has gotten people.

Example of An Offer Stack

I am now a freelancer. I charge e-commerce stores $5000/month to implement the Email Domination funnel (random name off the top of my head).

When I am on a sales call with the decision-maker of this e-commerce store, they may have objections about the price, OR just not be able to afford it.

SO, I now have a backup offer. I can implement a piece of the Email Domination Funnel for half the price ($5000 one-time fee). Rather than the entire funnel, I write specific sequences and hand them off to the store.

If this is still too much, I can offer to consult for $2500. 8 calls and I teach them how to implement the entire Email Domination Funnel by themselves. They get all of the value of the $5000/month service at a fraction of the cost.

At this point, $2500 one time fee seems like NOTHING compared to $5000/month.

Example For Coaches

First offer: The Actualization Program ($5000)

Full-fledged 3-month program.

Second offer: The Accelerated Program ($2500)

Accelerated 1.5 month program. Same value \+ material, half the time and half the calls (still extremely appealing).

Third offer: The Micro Program ($500)

2 weeks of DM or Telegram access, no calls. You assign them content from the program and talk them through it.

Now, once they go through any of these programs, you can upsell them on a micro coaching monthly retainer. $500/month with little time investment on your end. Let your mind run wild and get creative with this.

---

# Standing Out From The Competition (Your USP)

In short, your USP is what you have that competitors don’t.

Depending on the market, this could be as simple as serving one specific niche. I.E. a web design agency for coffee shops (this probably isn’t a very solid idea, but you get the point, there aren’t many other coffee shop exclusive web design agencies.)

If the market is more sophisticated/saturated with an offer similar to yours \- that’s when we need to get creative.

Answer these questions and choose and start to brainstorm your USP:

What does your product/service have that your competitors dont? (we have not created our offer yet, we will do that in The Godfather Offer)  
Can you provide something exclusive to your target?  
Do you have celebrity credibility in your market? (I.E. you worked with Dwayne “The Rock” Johnson and got him into movie shape)  
Do you distribute differently than your competitors? (For digital offers: is the knowledge delivered in a different way?)  
Can you offer lower prices OR higher quality

If you are having trouble brainstorming how YOU are different, here are some examples of successful USPs:

TOMS Shoes \- A child in need gets a new pair of shoes for every purchase you make.

Nerd Fitness \- A fitness website exclusively for “nerds”

Head & Shoulders \- Clinically proven to reduce dandruff

Dominos Pizza \- Hot and fresh pizza delivered to your door in 30 minutes or less  
Piece Together Your USP

Option 1: Take the greatest benefit of your offer and GUARANTEE they will receive that benefit

FedEx example: Guaranteed overnight delivery

(Some people offer overnight delivery but don’t guarantee it)

Agency example: Guaranteed X amount of leads per month or your money back

(This guarantees the client makes more than they spend)

Option 2: Your niche combined with your product/service without inconvenience

You see a lot of freelancers / agency owners / coaches with this: I help \[niche\] get \[results\] through \[product/service\] without \[inconvenience that competitors have\]

Option 3: Throw your unique mechanism at the end of your USP from above as the way you help them achieve their desired result.

# Understanding What We've Learned So Far

This shit can get confusing if we don't understand the purpose behind what I'm teaching. So I want to clear things up.

Most people get this wrong \- and you may still get this wrong the first couple of times \- but that's fine. Iteration is the key to success in all things, especially online business.

The 3 Things I Teach Here:

Audience building \- we haven't touched on this too much yet. BUT our next training is on building a twitter audience taught by 6 figure twitter ghostwriter ﻿JK Molina﻿   
Marketing / Offer creation \- All previous posts in this channel have been about marketing. We want to understand this so we can start off on the right foot and have more time to iterate throughout our journey. (I am teaching this first as it will help start your audience building on the right foot)

This is where most people go wrong. Selling a landing page to a creator won't cut it nowadays. Selling the "Ebook Sales Machine" (a custom made funnel for ebook sellers) is much more enticing \- and you can charge much more.  
Sales / Persuasion \- Selling your offer through social media via DMs and funnels.

There may be more to this, but its not worth focusing on, especially right now.

If you can build an audience, create a half-decent offer, and understand even the basics of sales \- 6 figures/year is not far out of reach given some time.

Hell, if you understand offer creation and sales via DMs, you don't need to build an audience (however I do recommend it, it's digital real estate)

One thing to note: you can use this information Im giving you to become a marketing consultant. A lot of people have crappy marketing. I personally sell what I am teaching you for $4k-$8k to creators.

Where Your Focus Should Be:

Do you have skills/knowledge? Do you understand a skill like landing page design, email marketing, copywriting, etc. well enough to help people improve theirs?

Yes? Craft your offer and start reaching out to people.  
No? Start learning like MAD here or via courses/YouTube/learning platforms.

Have you been in the fitness game long enough to get results for yourself? Want to become a coach? Nobody is stopping you besides yourself.

Same goes for any other form of coaching. Mindset, business, habits, relationships, productivity, anything.

If you understand offer creation/marketing/sales \- you can sell anything to anyone. (Because it genuinely helps them solve a problem.)

Once you understand a tad more than the basics/fundamentals \- START TAKING ON REAL WORLD PROJECTS.

Offer free/cheap work to your target audience. Start building landing pages. Start coaching friends and family. Start writing a book and give it to people. Get your name out there.

That is where your focus should be right now.

If you need any more clarity on this, please don't hesitate to ask your questions in \#Business Strategy.

# Market Sophistication, Customer Awareness, and Research

The final post in our market research series\! This post, along with the last 2, are necessary.

By simply having these in mind you will eliminate most competition. I also have more in the arsenal to eliminate competition further.

Your Target's Market Sophistication

You need to think about your marketing in the right context. You need to be able to pivot your messaging according to the market sophistication.

The 5 stages of market sophistication was coined by Eugene Schwartz, an elite marketer.

Stage 1: Brand new market \- you don’t really need to worry about this one. This is when there is no competition, but this is rare nowadays.

Stage 2: There are some competitors in this market \- but it is easy to stand out with your claims/promises (by being more specific and quantifiable than the rest with your promises/solutions). Chances are you don’t have to worry about this stage either.

Stage 3: More competition and better claims. This is where most markets live, and probably where yours does. Everyone is being bombarded with offers. You need to position yourself correctly (unique selling point and unique machine).

Stage 4: A ton of competition, having unique mechanisms, and large competitors emerge (Gurus, Apple, Tech Companies). You don’t need to worry about this stage too much. At this point you need to get creative with your marketing and show them how it works. You will learn to do this.

Stage 5: This is just a sea of competitors. The loudest and most valuable brands stand out.

It will ALWAYS be better to market to the stage your market is in or HIGHER.

You can determine your market’s level of sophistication by researching in the places we mentioned previously (FB groups, Amazon Reviews, Answer The Public).

The more content/people/amount of offers there are, the more sophisticated your market. Are they excited or tired of the products being pushed to them?  
Your Target's Level of Awareness

There is no “right way” to tweet, write a blog post, or write an email, launch an ad each and every time.

Your goal is to speak to specific people within their given awareness level.

The best way to think about it is by looking at your brand through your target’s eyes.

The Buyer’s Journey \- 5 Stages of Customer Awareness

Stage 1: Unaware. People won’t buy from you here. They don’t know who you are or what you sell. They don’t know they have a problem and that there is a solution for it.

Stage 2: Pain aware. They understand they have a problem but aren’t aware of a solution.

Stage 3: Solution aware. They know they have a problem and that there is a solution but they do not know about your solution.

Stage 4: Product aware. They know about your product but just haven’t bought it yet.

Stage 5: Most aware. People know you and your brand, they trust you. All it takes is a bit of scarcity to push them over the edge (discount or limited time offer).

We talked a bit about this in Solopreneur Foundations with your funnels/email sequences. Your "top-of-funnel" content (tweets, posts, videos) should focus on phases 1-3. Then you work them through your emails/backend funnel to introduce them to your product.

Now is your time to start researching current products/services in the marketplace. Take note of them \- you can use them to create better offers and “steal” ideas from them.

If you currently have an offer, now is the time to think about how you should actually be promoting.

Are you going straight out of the gate asking people to buy in stage 1? Or are you capturing a lead and nurturing it into stage 5?  
Research Your Ideal Customer

Based on your market’s level of sophistication and the majority of your targets’ awareness levels, answer the questions below.

These will be absolutely critical when creating your offer, writing copy, creating social posts, ANYTHING.

Most people shoot in the dark with this stuff, you want to be brutally aware of what your audience/potential customers are going through.

If you can, try to find these answers from REAL people on the internet. If you can’t, well... that's even more reason to start growing an audience or getting active in communities.

Important: Since you are probably looking for clients on social media \- the BEST form of market research is to offer free help in the DMs and get them on a call.

On this call, you can ask the questions below or other questions you have about their life / business. From there, you can give advice and start to make connections to implement in your offer.

Questions to answer about your target:

What is the typical story of this person that would buy what you plan on offering?  
Why do they buy it?  
What is their mindset towards their problem?  
What would make them buy your offer?  
What results do they hope they get?  
What have they done before to solve this problem?

Questions to answer about yourself:

Chances are you are selling something related to what YOU are good at. You may have purchased a similar/related product, or you have had these questions pop into your mind while learning.

The questions below are from Jose Rosado (a previous mentor of mine). Check him out on Twitter @joserosado.

What was your mindset then?  
Why did you buy it?  
What results were you hoping to get?  
What problem of yours were you trying to solve?  
What did you struggle with?  
What were your biggest “aha” moments?  
What were your objections?  
What stopped you from buying?  
What do you wish you had done differently  
What do you hope to do differently?

Answer those questions, save this in your Google drive, and start thinking deeply about your marketing.

# Narrowing Further \+ The Start of Market Research

Preface: brother Torbjørn Husevåg had a great question on the last post that should be discussed here.

Torbs question:

How would you describe the niche market / persona of this community in once sentence? Online solo entrepreneurs interested in financial, mental and physical development? 

My response:

It gets wonky with a personal brand, and this is moreso for fun/community rather than trying to scale and make a shit ton of money

In this case, since my ideas, thoughts, and personality are my main marketing "firepower"

My niche is me.

People that have the same interests, desires, problems that I can help them with through the experience I've gained

I put this text towards the end, "If you are building a personal brand, or theme account \- you need to take audience first vs product first into account. Which we will talk about later. You MAY not want to niche down a crazy amount."

Modern Mastery isn't very niched down, and for that reason \- I either need an audience (which I have) or I need to make it a big name (which I am planning to do)

If you want to start making sales and charging high prices from the start \- that is when this comes into play \- and is what many of my other offers are composed of

This should help today's lesson make more sense.  
Finding Your Target

This is where our research begins and how we find pain points/problems that we can use as firepower for creating a solution and attracting the right people.

Where to research:

Facebook groups: you can join groups in ANY niche. Bodybuilding (health), picking up chicks on Tinder (relationships), marketing for personal brands (wealth)

Start requesting to join some in your niche and pay attention to people that are asking questions (people that need help with specific problems)

Keep a running market research Google doc for all of this. You WILL NOT remember it in your head. Copy and paste everything.

Amazon Reviews: Specifically the books section. There are books on literally EVERY topic in almost every niche.

Find a popular book in your niche and read the 2-4 star reviews. These will tell you what was MISSING from the actual product \- that is how you can make yours better.

Again, write all of this down and start connecting the dots.

1 and 5 star reviews are mostly worthless as they don't give feedback, they are either angry or happy with the product.

Answer The Public: I do not have the most experience in this as I rely on the other methods \+ my audience on social, but it can be very powerful. I would recommend playing around on the website and possibly watching videos on how others use it.

Social Media: Same with facebook groups. Look for questions that people are asking or areas where people are struggling. Facebook groups gives you access to an audience \- this is another reason why building an audience is powerful.  
Painting Your Ideal Customer

Some may know this as a customer avatar \- it is very common in the marketing space because it is necessary.

These are the answers you are trying to find when you are going through the FB groups, amazon reviews, etc.

Copy/paste this into your Google doc and fill out the answers.

Btw, you are not limited to ONE customer avatar. You will be refining, iterating, and creating new ones for different products/services you create.

Age:

Gender:

What is their marital status? (Divorced, married, single, etc.)

Do they have children?

Where do they live?

What is their favorite quote?

What do they do for a living?

What is their annual income?

Did they graduate college?

What are their lifelong goals?

What are their values?

What are they are struggling with right now?

What are their major pain points relating to the niche you chose?

Where do they get their information from?

Books:  
Blogs/websites:  
Gurus:  
Social media:

What are some common objections/limiting beliefs to reaching their goals?

What does an average day look like for them?  
﻿  
﻿  
Specify Your Target

Write out a summary of your target.

Example: John is a 26-year-old college grad that became a financial advisor but he has a very hard time finding/attracting women into his life. He is worried that he is getting too old for the dating market.

This is who you are marketing to. Do not get too caught up on the actual ideal customer \- pay close attention to their deep, biological, and burning problems.

In our next lesson we will talk about market sophistication and levels of customer awareness (this was briefly discussed in the Solopreneur Foundations training, we will dive a bit more in depth here).

# The Start To Finding A Profitable Problem

By now you have probably heard of 'niching down' and targeting a specific group of people. That is what we will discuss.

This is absolutely necessary for any online business (regardless of how much you niche down). You won't be able to target their pain points and present your offer as a solution any other way.

You are also using this to target people you WANT to work with, especially if you are a consultant or freelancer. Life is better when you work with people you enjoy.  
Step 1: Choosing A Market

There are 3 main markets: health, wealth, and relationships.

These are where most profitable problems lie. Think about it... having problems in these areas are human nature.

BUT, you can't just solve the "wealth" problem as a whole.

"I will help you acquire wealth" sounds nice, but we need to get more specific, especially since we are solopreneurs, not huge corps.

Start with a market you have experience in or are interested in exploring.

We will choose health for this example.

Note: there are other markets. But, I do not have experience in them nor do I think they serve the purpose of this group.  
Step 2: Choosing A Submarket

For our health market, here are some example submarkets:

Resistance training  
Nutrition  
Yoga  
Mobility  
Medical fields

Again, choose one that you have experience in or are interested in.  
Step 3: Niche Market

Now, we narrow down further (this makes it easier to research, find specific problems, and create specific solutions)

Examples of niche health markets:

Bodybuilding supplements / sleep supplements / etc  
Bodybuilding training regimens  
Hot yoga  
Crossfit

If you are building a personal brand, or theme account \- you need to take audience first vs product first into account. Which we will talk about later. You MAY not want to niche down a crazy amount.

For freelancers and agencies, the more specific the better.

Next post we will talk about researching this market.

Both of these will be necessary to craft an offer/solution FOR that market.

I encourage you to start niching down based on your current experience and interests.

Take the time to research this further if you have to \- that is what will truly help you learn it.

# What You NEED To Understand For Your Social Media Business

I want to get this out of the way real quick and set a foundation for some of the things you will learn here.

If you are on Twitter (which ALL of you are if you joined this group early), you understand the whole ebook dilemma.

Grow an audience with basic tweets and sell an ebook to get rich\!

I'm not one to demonize this, it has its place, but it does create a limit on what you can sell and how much you can sell.

We are here to build something sustainable as a digital product creator, thought leader, consultant, freelancer, solopreneur, etc.

Here is some of what you need to know. This may not make sense to you right now, but trust me, it will.

Offer Creation 

You need to understand that you are not just selling a product or service. 

You are exchanging value (service/productized service) for value (money) 

You need to make your offer SEEM as valuable as possible to your buyer. The value you provide should OUTWEIGH the value they provide. AKA your offer should seem like a worthy investment to them. No matter if it is $300 or $30,000 

You do this by: 

Knowing WHO you are selling to (your customer avatar, must be able to afford what you plan to charge)   
Doing deep research on this avatar to understand their emotional triggers and pain points   
Showing them the PATH, how to get from point A to point B (how are you helping them transform?)   
Being unique through your positioning, unique selling proposition, marketing angle, and path (same as above, your path should be crafted for your avatar)   
Having proper risk reversal (think money back guarantee or "if I don't get X results than I will refund you your money," or "the length of service is 3 months, but I will work with you until we reach X result, if we do not hit it in 3 months")   
Using bonuses and discounts WISELY and to your advantage for negotiation   
Creating tiers of your offer for upsells and downsells (offer stacking)   
Pricing\! Making sure the price reflects the value you provide for the audience you provide to 

Most of you will be selling consulting services based on the contents of your ebook. Expanded, more in-depth, with built-in accountability to actually make it work.

The Basic Social Media Funnel 

Most of your funnels will look like this 

Post lead magnet or ebook to twitter   
Put buyers into a "buyers journey" email sequence (helping them utilize your ebook to the best of their ability)   
\-- If its a lead magnet \- you should put them in a welcome sequence, then sales sequence for your ebook, then buyers \-\> buyers journey \-\> appointment sequence   
Put buyers into an appointment sequence   
\-- Handling objections about your consulting offer, giving out some of your "secrets," using your copywriting knowledge and getting them on a call with you   
Send them to a qualification form to schedule a call   
Getting on a discovery/sales call with qualified buyers   
Sealing the deal

Inbound/Outbound Prospecting 

You should already be making connections on social media and HOPEFULLY you are attracting an audience that fits the bill for your offers (if you want to grow an audience). 

Without going into too much detail for inbound: 

People will DM you for help   
You can write tweets promoting your offer to DM you   
You pre-qualify them via questions regarding where they work/what they do   
You ask what they are struggling with relating to what YOU can help them with   
You offer to give them advice and talk about your offer via a phone call   
Send calendar booking, follow sales process, close 

For OUTBOUND: 

Same DM process to get them on a call   
You start conversations with people that fit the bill of your ideal customer   
You DM people that RT or comment on your posts as they have expressed some form of interest   
You can keep a prospecting list of ideal customers as a twitter "list," start engaging with them so they get familiar with your face. 

All of this sets the stage for what we will be talking about in here.

A lot of this was also covered in the first Solopreneur Foundations training. You HAVE to understand this and keep it in mind at all times so you don't head in the wrong direction.

MOST of your "high ROI" tasks will revolve around these 3 things.

---

# (For Creatives) Build An Audience & Land Clients At The Same Time

This post will not be for everyone.

It will work best for:

Web designers  
Graphic designers  
Brand designers  
Video editors

And anyone else that has an offer that can be visually displayed on social media.

This can be used by others, but you'll have to get creative with how you go about it.

However, everyone should go through the Advanced Marketing Roadmap and Customer Acquisition Roadmap so your offer is as good as it can get before you do this (and so you can close clients).

The problem with a lot of creative, design, or visual offers:

It is difficult to provide a compelling guarantee, risk reversal, or quantifiable promise unless stacked with another skill.

Like how with web design, you can promise more leads, but that doesn't hold much weight.

And when you study something like funnel creation, you probably won't be offering full websites anymore because you know you can create something better (something that gets direct results).

So, here's what you do.

1\) Pick Someone You Would LOVE To Work With

This is important.

This isn't direct outreach where we can reach out to everyone with little manual work.

You will have limited shots at this, but if you get it right, it will be worth it.

This works best on someone with a lot of followers, but not so much that they don't even log on social media.

Your best bet is to aim for someone with 10K to 200K followers, more or less. Test it out.

2\) Create Something For Them (And Make It HIGH QUALITY)

If you're a web designer, make them a website, landing page, or linktree style page.

If you make clips for TikToks, make it unique. Don't do the same old crappy captions and click bait sounds. Study their brand and make something they can't ignore.

If you are a logo designer, create a logo or illustration for their brand, course, or something else.

Do your best work here.

Even if the person you are making it for doesn't like it – you can use it as a portfolio piece to show people in a similar niche.

3\) Post It To Your Account And Tag Them

Post a screenshot, image, or video of what you made.

Tag the person you made it for in the post.

Something as simple as "Hey @username, I made this for you. Hope you like it." with the image attached.

Be genuine and non-salesy, as that will dictate whether they respond or not. You aren't aiming for the sale here, you are aiming for engagement.

Send them a link to your post in the DMs telling them if they like it, you can send it to them and they can use it for free. This will increase their likeliness of replying, retweeting, or sharing.

Why does this work?

The prospects may look bad if they don't respond to your post (they have public pressure to reply and make their brand look good)  
Their comment, retweet, or share will boost impressions and their audience will see it  
People that see the post will potentially comment and boost impressions further  
People that are interested in your work will reach out and ask for your rates

This way, you get eyes on your content, build authority, potentially make sales, and definitely gain some followers here and there.

If you can do this 1-2 times a week for 2-3 months, I can say with confidence that you will land a few clients.

Simple as that. No need to drag this one on longer than it needs to be.

Try it out and enjoy the rest of your day.

---

# How I Build Out Courses, Guides, Or Lead Magnets

I've had a lot of people ask for a guide on building out a course.

I hesitated writing a guide on it because there are so many different things to take into account:

What are you teaching?  
What format will best deliver that information? (Writing, video, ebook, emails, membership?)  
What are the limitations of the platform you are using to host the files?

At the end of the day, I feel like way too many people overcomplicate this (and for good reason).

You are packaging up knowledge, that you may not have full confidence in, and putting it out into a world of critics and uninformed opinions.

I really believe that is the main problem here.

So here's a brief guide before we dive into the actual guide:

Have an idea for the product  
Build it out however possible  
Launch it and practice dealing with the emotions that come with it

99% of people don't get to step 2 when that's what starts the momentum. It's difficult to stop building once you've started.

Now you have something to improve on. You can always change it. None of this is permanent. Your products evolve as you evolve if you are a personal brand.

If your products don't evolve, I would argue that you are not evolving as a person (and as others evolve, you are willingly staying in a market that is becoming more saturated).

Copying and emulating is the name of the game.

If you stagnate for too long, you will get copied out of business.

Enough of my mini-rant on "just doing it" and "figuring it out."  
Identifying A Personal or Professional Problem

I'm assuming that you already have an idea for a product.

If you don't have an idea, I would assume that you aren't ready to build out a product.

If you need ideas:

What is something that you do on a daily basis that you've improved?  
What problems do you have in your life right now that you can solve?  
How do those things intersect with your expertise or what you talk about on social media?

If your customer avatar is YOU, this becomes much easier. (This is how you earn an income by solving your own problems, Twitter becomes a public journal in a sense).

If your customer avatar is someone else like a business owner, you would be productizing your current service. You can go through everything in the Advanced Marketing Roadmap to nail this down.

With a personal brand, you are continually refining your professional skill set:

Copywriting (getting conversions and engagement)  
Social media growth (sending traffic)  
Email marketing (newsletter or sequences)  
Web design (personal site or blog)  
Graphic design (profile pic and banner)  
Any other professional skill that you talk about or teach on social media

You are also understanding your personal skill set:

Self-improvement  
Mindset and emotional control  
Health and fitness  
Spiritual health  
Communication and social dynamics  
Any other personal skill that you talk about or teach on social media

Throughout your entirety of growing your brand, you will gravitate toward a specific set of skills that you want to become good at.

Some people will spend more time studying and teaching mindset while others will study and teach social media growth.

Having a foot in all of these things gives you SO MUCH leverage that most people don't realize.

These combinations give you a unique of positioning your product down the road.

Now, take some time to brainstorm and braindump journal about problems you've solved for yourself or potential problems you can solve.

Are you a great twitter thread writer? How did you get to that point?

Are you calm and collected all the time? What problem is associated with that and how did you solve it?

Do you suck at writing newsletters? That's a problem. Can you get really good at writing newsletters and document the process?

Take some time to write out the things you are good at, bad at, and the common problems associated with those.  
Testing A System

Systems sell.

The creator economy is actually The Systems Economy.

How can you start testing a system after you've identified a problem?

Notion.

Why Notion? Because it is becoming more and more popular. It is a great way of building out systems for things you do on a daily basis.

It makes it easy to visualize how you solve a specific problem.

(It also acts as an outline for building out a curriculum AND is a cool bonus for your customers).

Based on the problem you identified:

Educate yourself on how to solve it through free online resources, your prior experience, or other courses that can act as inspiration  
Start building out step-by-step processes in Notion that make it easier on you to solve the problem  
Test that process on yourself and refine it as roadblocks come up

Example:

I was never consistent with writing newsletters and always saw them as a daunting task.

From there I could:

Research how to write better long-form content  
Take notes and start practicing  
Create a Notion template that reminds me of the principles and other tips that helped me  
Get results with my newsletter and use that as social proof for the product

I've done this multiple times inside MMHQ.

There are fitness training programs, thread writing guides, and a few other things that are based off of a Notion template.

The curriculum becomes pretty easy to create after that.

What can this Notion system be used for?

An MVP of a SaaS you want to build in the future  
An incentive for testimonials or just to give away to people you are networking with (leading with value)  
What your course curriculum is built off of so they have an actionable way of practicing and implementing what you teach

This is yet another reason why I recommend documenting EVERYTHING in your life. Everything. Put it in Notion.

Your journal, monthly reflections, goals, vision, business SOPs, everything.

All of these can be turned or combined into a product in the future.  
Outlining The Curriculum

Always. Outline. Your. Projects. First.

I don't care if it's a product or just your weekly newsletter.

You are missing out on valuable information if you do not.

Start with a braindump.

Write down everything you would ever want to include in the course or product.

After that, outline course sections, modules, chapters, or whatever it may be.

Let it marinate.

Write down what you are aware of and let your subconscious give you ideas as you go about your week.

As ideas and inspiration come to you, immediately note it down and add it to the outline.

Once the outline feels somewhat complete, start building.  
Building Out The Curriculum

I like to take the "best of both worlds" approach and cover all of my bases.

I write out the entire curriculum, ebook, or guide.

I fill in the blanks, provide real-world examples, and walk people through the Notion systems in a Loom video.

You can create professional PowerPoint-style slides if you'd like (based off of your written curriculum, but Loom just makes it so easy to record your screen and show examples.

Depending on what product hosting platform you are using, you can either write the curriculum in Google Docs (for something like Gumroad) and export each section as a PDF.

Or you can write it all out in a membership dashboard like Kartra or Teachable which makes it easy to separate everything out into modules.

Then, you can download, upload, and/or embed the Loom videos in the respective place inside whatever platform you are using.

It is a tad difficult to go into more specifics than just this (because everyone has different goals and areas of expertise), so I hope that was helpful.

If you have any questions, never hesitate to post them in the business-strategy or writing-and-idea-generation channel\!

If you want 1 on 1 help with all of this, shoot me a DM on Discord to discuss my Digital Consciousness Consulting that I am starting up (it's expensive, but I guarantee brand growth and sales).

Talk soon🤝
