# The Purpose Of A Tripwire Offer

A tripwire is a low-cost product that gauges seriousness and interest.

It is a piece of your product offerings that is low commitment and leads into your next product well.

Previously, Websites That Work was a $17 tripwire for my $97 Web Design Wealth (now High Ticket Essentials).

I started out my journey with only WDW, and when I started piecing my email marketing together, I put Websites That Work in a sequence before it. Those that bought WTW were much more likely to buy WDW.  
The Purpose Of A Tripwire

If you have a product or service AND are building an audience — you are guaranteed to have people in your audience that do not want to buy your offer.

So, what can you do? Teach them what is necessary to use your offer. You need to create customers in a sense.

A tripwire:  
Is usually positioned to beginners. Your audience is 95% beginners.  
It is low cost but not free — meaning you have higher quality emails and customers. Buyers are more likely to buy again.  
Raises customer level of awareness surrounding a problem that your main product or service solves.  
Builds trust in you and your future products (so make your tripwire high quality, overdeliver).  
Where Does A Tripwire Go In Your Funnel?

You can sell it directly on the timeline of course, but in your email funnel it goes in between your welcome sequence and main sales sequence.

Ryan Deiss calls this Engagement, but he doesn't limit it to a tripwire. It can be a sequence dedicated to engaging your subscribers.

In this case it can be a free guide related to your product simply to educate them and see if they are interested in that topic (so you know if you should put them in your sales sequence).

I prefer adding a small price tag to guage their seriousness, so it is a tripwire.  
I Recently Created A Tripwire — Here Are The Results

I have been planning on building out a new product (The 2 Hour Creator or something like that).

An idea came to mind to start building out more of the funnel for that product.

A $7 product that would lead both into MMHQ and the new product.

I called it 7 Days To Genius Ideas and positioned it toward beginners.

BOTH those that are already creating content, and those who just want to form a creative habit (so I can show them how simple it is to turn ideas into content).

Do you see how I am raising the awareness levels of my audience?

I am showing them that creating content, a product, or service is as simple as consistently executing on good ideas — so I help them have better ideas that separates them from everyone else.

I launched on a whim the other day — and the results were pretty surprising.

20% of the people that bought the tripwire purchased an MMHQ subscription (if you are reading this — whats up\! I hope you enjoy the transparency I strive for).

And that was only after the first day. I structured it as a challenge. More may join towards the end of that challenge.

Why did they join MMHQ after purchasing the product?  
I gave them a quick win by helping them have a "Genius Idea"  
I told them what they can use that idea for (content, product, or service)  
I positioned MMHQ as a way that helps with that  
Should You Create A Tripwire?

The answer: probably.

Do you have a current product or service that you are selling?  
Have you built out any email sequences yet?  
Does your audience have people that aren't ready for your main product or service yet?  
Can you target those people and educate them enough to be ready for your product or service? (that is, improve them to a point of having better problems that your main offers solve?)  
Would a tripwire fit your offer stack / value ladder to perfection?

As a reminder, here is what a solid value ladder looks like.

Lead magnet that you promote on the timeline to get email subscribers  
(Add the tripwire here if you'd like, it's optional)  
Main product that is a "Do It Yourself" version of your high ticket offer  
High ticket offer that is a Done With You consulting or Done For You freelance offer.  
(You can eventually do super high ticket retreats or seminars if you'd like, again, optional)

Then, once you have all of those fleshed out via the Email Marketing Roadmap, all you have to do is focus on creating content, growing your social media, and plugging your lead magnet.

Then, the other products sell without people knowing it.  
Something new — I just recently got a testimonial software. If you've enjoyed your time here in MMHQ, I'd love to hear about it here.

As always, if you have any questions, leave them in the \#business-strategy channel\!

# The Sales Page Copywriting Framework

I am not a professional copywriter, nor have I done it for freelance work — but I have seen great success with my sales pages.

I have taken copy courses, gotten tips from freelance copywriters, and have tested numerous ways of crafting sales pages. What you will find below is a streamlined way of doing so.

Start to think of your sales page as a way of structuring your marketing strategy. You will be trying to effectively communicated your offer and all of your marketing firepower from the Advanced Marketing Roadmap.

Persuasive Writing Structures

There are 3 writing structures I want you to keep in mind.

AIDA  
Attention, Interest, Desire, Action  
PAS  
Problem, Agitate, Solution  
PASTOR \- read more here  
Problem, Amplify, Story/Solution, Transformation/Testimony, Offer, Response

The common theme with these is using psychological triggers to keep the reader engaged, communicate the value of your offer, and make them convert.

While I do not treat any of these as law, you should keep their general structure in mind.

Is your headline holding attention?   
Are you painting a picture of their big problem(s) relating to your solution?   
Are you agitating / amplifying that problem?   
Do you have a soft story / transformation that relates to their situation?   
Do you introduce your offer / solution in an enticing way?   
Do you have a strong call to action?   
Are you holding the readers attention up until that call to action?

How To Write Your Copy

As with most things, I would highly HIGHLY recommend brain dumping beforehand. Do not try to write the final draft in one go.

Outline, brainstorm, go about your life, let your subconscious work on your copy for you, and take note of things that come to mind as you go about your days.

This is especially true for your headlines, lead, and offer introduction. Write down as many ideas as you can. Force them out of your head. Then come back to them a few days later with more subconscious ammunition.  
The Hero Section (Above The Fold)

There are 4 aspects of a great hero section. For this entire "Hero Section" you will be including as much of your marketing firepower as possible.

A reminder of your marketing firepower:

Your USP  
Your quantifiable end result (or timeframe if you have trouble with QER)  
Your promise / solution  
Your target audience (calling them out catches attention)  
A hint at your unique system/mechanism  
The big problem  
Risk reversal / guarantee

It is up to you to treat these as puzzle pieces, brainstorm, and piece together the perfect hero section using these 4 things:

1\) The Eyebrow (optional)

The eyebrow is the optional text above your headline. Usually small and hardly noticeable. This is where I like to call out my target audience.

2\) The Headline

This is the most important aspect of all of your copy. I typically like to include my promise/solution, aspects of my USP, my QER, and a brief mention of one of their problems.

3\) The Subheadline

I use the subheadline to touch on anything else I missed. Mostly the risk reversal and unique mechanism.

4\) The CTA Button

It only makes sense to have a call to action button in this area. It looks good and gives people the option to buy upfront if they are ready.

Example:

Can you guess how I pieced everything together for the MMHQ copy? Take a second to look at the hero section and see how I pieced things together.

Please keep in mind that MMHQ is a community based around my audience. It has many moving pieces that are a tad difficult to structure in my copy well. If you have a hyper-focused info product, this becomes 10x easier (and you probably shouldn't treat my copy as the greatest way of doing things — compare to a similar product / service as yours).

The Lead

The lead section is where you introduce the problem and agitate it. This can be very simple or complex. Here are 2 things you can include:

1\) Social Proof

I have seen great copywriters recommend including social proof up front. I think it is a smart move IF you have a lot of social proof. It builds trust from the beginning and can be used to handle initial objections.

Include 2-3 strong testimonials.

2\) The Lead

My favorite way of doing this is simple. Bullet points.

When in doubt, bullet points are your best friend. I see it as a way of hitting multiple pain-points and painting a picture of where they are currently at.

It is like a list-style tweet — if people relate with one point, they will like, retweet, and possibly follow (they will keep reading your copy).

The key to these is to get as specific as possible. Dig into your market research from the Advanced Marketing Roadmap. Dig into your past experiences. Brain dump and iterate on what you write down.

Of course, if you need to, have a few sentences before and after the lead to transition nicely from the hero section and into the body.

The Body

The body section is where you include your story, transformation, and solution. This can be in the form of a personal story, a specific client success story, or just a brief explanation of the solution.

I wouldn't overcomplicate this section too much. It does not have to be a certain character or word count.

However, I would try to handle as many objections as possible while telling this story. Refer back to your market research, understand what is going through your customer's mind as they are reading, and handle their objections in your copy.

At the start of this body section you should include a headline. I treat headlines as the big idea behind the entire section. In short, summarize the most compelling points of the body section as the headline.

If your body talks about a client that went from overweight to having a six-pack, your headline could be: How John Lost His Love Handles While Eating Pizza Everday

The Offer Introduction

From what I've heard, your offer introduction should take up no more than 20% of your landing page. (That is, 20% of the \~600 words it will take to get to the end of the main call to action).

As with all major sections in your copy, include a headline at the start. Something as simple as "Introducing \[Product Name\]" works fine.

Keep this brief, use benefits rich language, use bullet points, and use the bullet points in your lead to generate ideas on how to best word these. Your offer introduction should act as a solution to the problems you listed in your lead.

Another thing — you should run through your product / offer outline and write down what the reader actually wants out of each section. Benefits over features.

If you have an ebook and one chapter is on "how to count calories and be in a caloric deficit"

You should write it as: The stupid simple way of guaranteeing weight loss (even if you were to eat a big mac everyday)

You can think of these bullets as mini-headlines. With that, I would study how people write headlines. Watch some YouTube videos and read blog articles on it.

After you introduce different aspects of your offer, you can include another section of bullet points where you introduce the bonuses that come along with it.

Social Proof

Again, have another headline. "Praise From Our 500+ Customers" or something along those lines work.

Then, of course, list off all of the social proof you have. If you don't have any, don't worry — but make it your full time job to get social proof.

Call To Action

The call to action is not as simple as a button. There are multiple things you can include here.

1\) Display Of Value

I like comparing the value of what I am offering to what is currently on the market. Are you giving away information that usually costs more?

Can you break down the what they get relating to the price? (If you are offering a solution to getting a six pack, paint a picture of what that is worth to someone... is a $47 investment worth having your wife look at you with googly eyes?)

Here is an example from the MMHQ landing page:

2\) Giving Them 2 Options

Remind yourself of the main points in your lead (the pain points) and the main points of your offer (the benefits / solution).

Paint a brief picture of where they are now, and give them the option to stay where they are or transform their life.

How you word this is up to you. You don't want to be like, "You can either keep your sh\*tty life or buy my product and change it."

That's just going to lose conversions lol. Have some self-awareness and toy with it a bit.

That's It\! (Kinda)

If you are writing copy for a Gumroad landing page, you can stop here.

Your main call to action should come quick. Display your value with the info above in about 500-700 words and end it there (Gumroad doesn't allow more than one call to action).

If you are creating a page on Carrd, WordPress, or another software that allows you to have CTA buttons anywhere — you can end the copy here or consider it extra.

Now we can dive into the extras that come after the main call to action.

Frequently Asked Questions

Everything that comes after is about objection handling and possibly hitting different marketing angles for those that are unsure about your offer.

FAQ's are pretty straightforward, but the questions should be crafted in a persuasive way.

Bonus Headlines and Sections

You can continue this page for as long as you want with call to action buttons spaced out.

I typically use these to write down more stories, handle objections, target different levels of awareness and include anything that I feel is persuasive.

I can't really teach you how to write these sections. That is completely dependent on your marketing and offer.

If you need inspiration for this or want to see an example, check out the MMHQ landing page (but again, understand that it is a community and I am doing my best to display its value. Your product will most likely be more streamlined with a specific end result.)

# The Greatest Lead Generation & Leverage System

A personal brand is not a "business..." it is a lead generation and leverage system.

The nature of social media relies on individual experiences to grow and gain authority. Per the Social Matrix.

In short, personal branding is a long-term game. Your personal brand is a lead generation mechanism like no other. You are nurturing potential customers long-term (potentially for the rest of your life if you enjoy the work that you don't want to outsource.)

Direct response marketing is a short-term immediate selling game (that gets your loyal fans to make a purchase).

This is very difficult to replicate with cold emails, cold DMs, etc etc. NOBODY CAN REPLICATE YOU.

People do not choose to follow your cold emails or DMs.

Building a personal brand will have people wanting to work with you whether you are good at selling or not. Now imagine when you ARE good at selling. Double whammy.

Bigger Is Better For Brands

There is one common theme for personal brands that nobody seems to take into account.

Everyone is building a BRAND rather than an agency, coaching, or freelancing business.

You don't see any agency accounts on social media trying to land clients. There are some, but who wants to follow a business account that just tries to sell you the whole time?

You see individuals on social media that use their experience to land clients for their agency (or coaching, freelancing, ecom store, or product sales.

Why is bigger better? MORE LEVERAGE & NOT PUTTING YOURSELF IN A BOX.

As Naval said:

"Fortunes require leverage. Business leverage comes from capital, people, and products with no marginal cost of replication (code and media)."

A personal brand can cover many of those bases. Primarily, "people."

That is, building an audience by producing content.

Then, creating digital products or SaaS based around your interests, things you talk about, and problems you solve. (code and media)

As Jack Butcher said:

"Build distribution, then build whatever you want."

The cool thing about this is that your personal brand can pivot and sell anything in the Big 3:

Health  
Wealth  
Relationships  
If you end up hating fitness, sweet \- you can slightly rebrand to something that interests you without destroying your entire business.

If you end up transitioning out of freelancing or client work (like I did) \- you can slightly rebrand as well.

Same goes for everything.

We are building a personal brand for cash flow and fulfilling work, not to sell it like a business. This should give you the opportunity to pursue your interests at any time. Then, if you want to fuel a 'sellable' business down the road with your personal brand's cash flow, easy peasy.

People care about the person behind the ideas, not the ideas.  
Your job is to:

Grow via posting about your experiences in an engageable way   
See: Social Matrix, Master Swipe File, The Legacy Beginner Course, and most of the content in Social Media Strategy  
Get in the habit of bettering yourself and consuming GOOD content   
Set aside time for idea generation (listening to podcasts, reading books, getting content from OUTSIDE of social media so you aren't posting the same things as others)  
Give yourself time.   
Money loves speed, but socials love experience.  
The information, money, trial & error, and life experiences in general compound over time into an incredible personal brand. This may sound silly, but you will only understand this through experience.

Example: I wrote my ebook The Path To Power at the start of my Twitter journey. My new brand Modern Mastery is THE EXACT SAME PHILOSOPHY. I'm just much better at getting my message across now.

"Play iterable games." as Naval said.

Hit publish on the things in life / business that will make you look back 1 year from now and cringe at your work.

You Must Be "Interesting"

Interesting does not mean traveling the world, being surrounded by women, and living in mansions. Sure, this is interesting and does well, but is unrealistic to most.

If you have the time, I would highly recommend studying mimetics \- why humans desire specific things.

In short \- people hop on the bandwagon. If you are enjoying something and sound like you have experience with it, they will want to enjoy it too.

This is why it is important to be confident in what you post \+ have strong convictions. Everyone is second-guessing themselves every second of the day. They will follow your steps if you are confident in your life choices. 

(And this will bring them the most results, even if they fail. At alteast they failed fast in one direction).

The thing with conviction \- what you believe now isn't what you will believe down the road. This is fine. Your content, audience, and self will evolve the longer you are in the game. Personal development \= business development.

How to be "interesting:"

Do things that the masses don't do, this can be as simple as:   
Going to the gym  
Skipping breakfast (haha)  
Drinking a specific kind of water (like San Pellegrino, a meme on Twitter)  
Building a business  
Literally anything that isn't mediocre.

Take note of ALL of the life choices you make and which ones are different than what others do.

I'm serious. What are the weird things that you do?

Do you eat Brazil nuts like Dr. Lagakos? Do you do your own kind of meditation (can you give that kind of meditation a name)? Do you make a smoothie everyday (like my enlightenment elixir)?

Take some time to think about this. This concept started to register with me by studying Matt Ogus' old videos. He used to have his Ogus Cake (an oatmeal cake) and Ogus Salad (a Chipotle bowl thrown on top of a bag of spinach).

The longer you are in the game, the better. You will start making more mental connections. Your quality of life will increase. Your skillset will improve. Online business \= personal development in the creator economy.

Putting Off The Right Energy

This is a weird phenomenon, but people can sense your energy in posts and are attracted to it.

This does not mean you have to be extremely energetic and hyped up all the time \- you simply have to be consistent with how you speak.

For myself, I aim for calm and insightful \- kind of like a philosopher \- because one of my goals in life is to be able to articulate my points like a philosopher. I want to achieve depth and impact.

This is incredibly difficult, if not impossible, to teach.

Study how accounts speak on all social platforms. The accounts that YOU vibe with the most. These will not be the same accounts other's like.

Doing this will turn you into an amalgamation of the top players in their space.

Creating a mood board for your brand has proven helpful in doing this well:

Find 1-2 scenic images on Google, Unsplash, or Pexels that represents your "vibe." (Think of your end goal \- what environment do you want to live in? What environment does your audience want to live in when imagining their future?)   
Examples:  
A cabin in a forest with dark tones (lumberjack vibe)  
A beach with palm trees (adventurous and serene vibes)  
Skyscrapers and cities (I use this \- because it represents structure and "big city living")  
Find 1-2 images of a human that shows your "vibe" \- like a customer avatar for yourself. If you want to choose an image from the accounts you want to emulate, that makes it easier. Be sure it matches the vibe you put off in real life.   
Examples:  
A stoic philosopher for deep thoughts and insights  
A bronze age bodybuilder for "the good life"  
A businessman in a suit near a rooftop pool  
Start thinking about what imagery attracts YOUR attention.  
Who do you follow on social media?  
What kind of lifestyle do they promote and what does it look like?

In essence, you are painting a picture of the lifestyle that YOU and your audience want to achieve. YOUR VISION.

Broad Catch, Specific Sale

With a personal brand, you are defining the vision, "why," and mission of the company.

In this case, YOU are the company. YOU are the niche.

You need to understand yourself to be able to effectively communicate your vision for others.

Your brand is what pulls in loyal followers that join in and spread your message.

When it comes to sales, direct response marketing is king. We have an entire roadmap on this (advanced marketing and offer creation), but for now understand that the two are different.

Direct response marketing is targeting one specific persona with one specific offer that solves one of their burning problems via emotional leverage.

Direct response is best used:  
In paid advertising  
In promotional tweets/content  
On your landing page  
In your sales emails  
Offer creation  
Cold outreach  
Direct response \= sales. You are trying to get an immediate action/conversion out of someone.

General marketing / Branding is what a wide range of people are attracted to. This is best used to gain loyal and fanatic followers (refer back to the Social Matrix to understand this deeper.

Think of it like this \- your brand is for showing them the lifestyle you are helping them work towards \- your sales are for giving them the tools to do that.

This is also an introduction to marketing angles and positioning.

I.E. If your brand promotes financial freedom \- you can sell a product/service on web design, philosophy, marketing, writing, or anything else that can be tied to financial freedom.

What you help them accomplish \+ what you've done and can teach that will help them get there (even if it's only a small step towards their desired end goal).

If you enjoyed this post \- consider giving MMHQ a shoutout on Twitter and tagging me in it. This helps a lot in terms of word-of-mouth marketing IF you truly enjoy it here.

If you have any questions, always feel free to pop them in \#business-strategy channel\!

---

# How To Write An Appointment Sequence

The final piece of the email marketing puzzle for a bit\! We could still talk about segmentation and affiliate sequences, but for now \- a great general structure for creators, coaches, and freelancers is to:

Have a lead magnet  
Put downloaders into an indoctrination sequence  
Then put them into a sales sequence for your tripwire or low ticket product  
Put them into an appointment sequence for your high ticket offer (this article)  
Tag subscribers that finish the sequences to send some form of consistent newsletter.

If you are unsure how to create these sequences, you can use ConvertKit (here is an article of how to set things up), or Kartra if you want an all in one platform.

Now, this will be my strategy that has worked for me in getting leads per my sales process. You should have your offer worked out, some form of lead generation and qualification process, and be ready to take on clients.

This appointment sequences make it easier to automate the lead generation process and work leads up the customer levels of awareness. This makes it easy to plug your lead magnet only and land clients. Once you have a large enough audience you can start to transition from DM outreach to this.

The Value Emails

This has a similar structure as a sales sequence. You don't want to ONLY be sending promotional emails or else people will get annoyed.

You need to have 3-4 value emails that discuss more advanced topics. Make people more and more aware of the BIGGER problem that your high ticket offer solves.

You should have this part on lock per the last articles on indoctrination and sales sequences.

The Offer Introduction Emails

For 1-2 emails, you will give people a complete rundown of your offer. Who it's for, what problem it solves, your STRONG risk reversal, a lot of social proof, and a strong call to action.

You want to reduce as much friction as possible with them clicking the link and expressing interest. I would recommend having an intake form without a link to schedule a call. Calls imply pressure and time. Read through this article to set up your qualification process.

With these 1-2 emails, you have to make sure they understand every aspect of your offer. Follow the Godfather Offer template and write it out compellingly using the PASTOR sales copy framework.

The Follow Up Emails

This is where the appointment sequence is different. THE MONEY IS MADE IN THE FOLLOW-UPS.

If you have sent cold outreach messages, you know this is the case. Email marketing is our way of automating this.

You will be sending quite a few follow-ups.

Start at 1 follow-up every 3 days for a week or two.

Then go up to 1 follow-up every week for 2-3 weeks.

Then 1 follow-up every 2 weeks for 2-3 weeks.

(After these follow-ups, I like to copy and paste my offer introduction email and remind them of everything that the offer consists of.)

Then 1 follow-up every month for 1-2 months.

People get busy. They need to be reminded of your offer and that it is a fit for them.

You can talk about different parts of your offer in these follow-up emails, or just ask if they are free for a call. You can test different angles as well.

That's it.

As a beginner, I wouldn't overcomplicate this. Get the emails written to the best of your ability. You can always go back and change them. That's the beauty of this... the "build once, sell twice" philosophy of Jack Butcher. You are building something that you can constantly iterate on.

If you have any questions regarding this article or want feedback on your own email ideas, post them in the \#business-strategy channel\!

---

# How To Write A Sales Sequence

This article is for those that have a lead magnet and some form of product to sell. If you have a service, this will work \- but I will be writing an article specifically for high ticket service sequences (since the sales process is different).

Your lead magnet should be putting people into an indoctrination sequence. Here is an article on how to write your indoctrination sequence \- and another article for how to set up your sequences in ConvertKit.

Once you have all of those, let's dive in:

The Problem Emails

As with everything in marketing, much of your content is based on raising people up the customer levels of awareness. Making them hyper-aware of their problems, proposing the benefits to solving them, and giving them the system for self-transformation.

If you have a product, you should have some idea of what problems you target audience is experiencing. If you haven't, you need to conduct market research. You can probably start to see why having a solid marketing strategy is absolutely necessary. It bleeds into all of your content, branding, promotions, and more.

The first 3-5 emails of your sequence are going to:  
Present valuable topics related to what you are selling  
Introducing the BIG problem that they are facing  
Making them understand how it's impacting their life (painting a picture of the worst-case scenario, negative visualization)  
Explaining a transformation they can undergo. Using your own or a previous customers' as an example.  
Doing this in the form of valuable emails that explain but don't show how. You can make people aware without explaining every little detail. (A good example of this is my previous email on the one-man business model. It is not a sales email, but is a good example of explaining and not showing.)  
You can think of these as blog posts, but they display your expertise related to your product. You are making them understand why they should do the same thing as you.

In the last 1-2 emails, you can leave a soft-sell at the end in the form of a P.S.

"If you are interested in \[ABC benefits or solving XYZ problems\] the check out \[name of course\] here."

This is kind of like a drawn-out and sales call. You are just automating it with email. Same things go for DMs. They are all sales. Sales sales sales.

These will also be used and condensed when it's time to sell.

By the time they hit your sales emails, they should be at level 4-5 of the customer awareness levels.

The Sales Emails

Now that they are aware of the problem they need to be solved, it's time to provide the solution for it.

The next 2-3 emails of the sales sequence:  
For a sales email, you should follow the general problem \> story \> offer introduction \> call to action while letting lose all of your marketing firepower.  
You can also follow the PASTOR framework for writing the email.  
Provide as much social proof as you can (one of these emails can even be "X got Y results" as the subject line. Then diving into the problem, explaining their transformation, and so on.  
By this point many of your subscribers will be at level 5 on the awareness level. They need some form of scarcity and urgency to buy.

Here's what you can do for scarcity:  
Have a discount for a limited time. Since this is an automated sequence, you will have to use something like Kartra which has countdown timers, or create a custom landing page with Carrd for your Gumroad product and use Deadline Funnel for evergreen countdowns.  
You will run this sale for 1-2 days and send reminder emails until it ends.  
If you are unable to do an automated countdown, you can add on a bonus or just have a discount without a timer.

Once you have your sales sequence in place, all you have to do is promote your newsletter or lead magnet on the timeline consistently and let people run through your sequences.

If you have any questions about this, drop a question in the \#business-strategy channel\!

---

# How To Write An Indoctrination Sequence

If you are considering writing an indoctrination sequence, you should have 1 of 2 things:

A lead magnet relevant to your product or what you talk about  
A simple email opt in page

Once you have these, you can use your email marketing software of choice (ConvertKit is good, I am using Kartra for everything). You can also use Gumroad Workflows, I made a tutorial on it here.

You will be putting the people that opt-in into this sequence.

Tangent: Start thinking of any digital product, free or paid, as an offer. Run them through this framework so you can get maximum signups and write better, more compelling copy.

The Welcome Email

In your welcome email, you should:  
Thank them for downloading your product or opting-in  
Tell them your brand's mission, the reasons you do what you do  
Tell them what they can expect in the next emails  
Ask them to reply telling you they got the email or downloaded the product (this helps with your email sender score)

The Story Emails

Your story emails are 1-2 emails that describe your transformation or a client's (or both). These help build authority and authenticity with your subscribers.

Your story emails should include:  
Where you started out. A position they can relate to. This builds trust (you can begin to introduce the problems(s) that your products/services solve per the customer levels of awareness)  
What sparked the change, the mentors you had, what you decided to dedicate yourself to, and why  
The resolution. How you fixed the problem and dug yourself out of the whole. Why it set you on the path you are on now

I personally split mine up into two emails. I introduced the low point of my life in the first, then a few more failures and resolution in the second.

You CAN end your indoctrination sequence here. Especially if they signed up for a newsletter only (so they don't get spammed with emails).

If you want to add more emails, here we go.

The Introductory Emails

I like to think of introductory emails as broad explanations of the topics you talk about. You can have 2-3 of these in your sequence.

Talk about the importance of the things you've learned along your journey and aided in your transformation. An introduction to your expertise and the things you teach.

If you are a web designer, introduce how web design can impact somebody's business.

If you are a fitness coach, introduce the importance of fitness in all aspects of life.

Etc.

Treat these as a blog post of sorts \- or any other structured long form content.

In copy: the lead (problem), the body (transformation, steps they can take), solution (the benefits it will have on their life.

The Golden Framework: what (setting the scene), how (steps to desired result), why (the emotion behind it).

This sets the stage for hitting hard on specific problems in their lives related to those topics when its time to have a sales sequence for your product / service.

Other Info

You can space these emails out as much as you'd like. I've normally spread them apart to go out every 2-3 days.

Most other things should not be overthought. You can test and iterate for your lifetime of entrepreneurship. Just get the sequence up and running so you can start promoting your opt in page\!

As always, if you have any questions, pop them in the \#business-strategy channel.

---

# Qualifying Prospects So You Don't Waste Time On Calls

I've had a few members ask about qualification, here is exactly how I do it.

This is for those that have a high ticket offer \- freelancing, coaching, consulting, or a high ticket course.

You should understand where this comes in the sales process.

First, you create your offer and run it through some of the marketing articles.

Then when it comes time to reach out to potential clients and get them on a call \- you will need to qualify them. Too many people get on calls with anyone and everyone just to find out that they genuinely can't afford their service. This wastes time. Wasted time \= wasted money.

Before you dive into this \- you should have something to sell, understand how to DM your target audience, qualify them (this post), then get on a sales call with them.

For a deeper explanation of all of the above \- check out the Sales Mastery Training with Andy Strohm.

Here is how you qualify your prospects.

The Traditional Method: Calendar link with qualifying questions

Downside \- you don't have much control over who schedules a call (you don't know if they can afford your services BEFORE the call is scheduled).  
Upside \- good for those that are under $10K per month and are going for sheer volume of calls from inbound/outbound DMs (don't have a built out funnel with consistent leads)

The Gym Salesman Method: Intake form (questionnaire) \> call the prospect \> close them or schedule another call

Downside \- the prospect may not answer the phone and you will have to follow up to schedule a call. You have to CALL while the lead is hot \- within 15-30 minutes after they fill out the form. Some people don't have that flexibility.  
Upside \- you can close the deals quick.

The Automated Method: Intake form \> information gets put into a Google sheet \> you or a commission-based closer can call them or DM them.

Downside \- you will need a consistent flow of leads from your social media audience / other promotional channels.  
Upside \- If you have a closer, it is hands off. You can also DM them with more qualifying questions or send them your calendar to schedule a call. (Sometimes you can just close them in the DMs.)

Your Sales Funnel

Let's keep this brief.

If you are DMing people and walking them through the DM script \- then you don't necessarily need a landing page describing your offer or running through the copywriting framework.

The main time you will need a landing page is for traffic that doesn't go through the DMs (your bio link, emails, or promotions on the timeline).

If you are DMing them \- send them straight to the intake form. If you aren't \- send them to your landing page that links to the intake form.

Your Intake Form

An "intake form" is just a fancy way of saying questionnaire. It will have qualifying questions and everything you need to take control of the sales call.

You will need 2 things \- a calendar (with form functionality) and a form software.

Calendly (free \+ paid) \- You will absolutely need a Calendly account. You will have to upgrade to add more questions and have more flexibility. You will need this whether you have a separate intake form or not.  
JotForm (free) \- You can create your intake form here for free and get email notifications for new leads. (Downside: I don't like the design of the forms).  
TypeForm (free \+ paid) \- A great-looking form with a lot of customizability and automation features.  
Google Forms (free) \- A classic solution that can pair with Google Sheets to capture your leads information.

Questions For Your Intake Form

I've told you time and time again to emulate what others in your niche are doing, this time is no different.

Find somebody who has a similar offer to you and swipe the questions they have on their intake form.

Here are some tried and true options:

First name, email, phone number, and social media handle  
What do you do for work? (soft qualification, you can judge their income)  
What is your motivation behind wanting X? (X \= the result / service you offer them)  
What is your current \[state\]? (where they are now in relation to your service)   
For marketing services \- \[state\] \= current monthly revenue  
For fitness coaching \- \[state\] \= fitness starting point  
For performance coaching \- \[state\] \= revenue or mental state  
What is your target \[state\]? (where they want to be through your service)  
Where would you like to see exponential improvement? (multiple choice with different aspects of what you offer)  
What are you struggling the most with in that area? (relating to the question above)  
How long have you been trying to get X results?  
On a scale of 1-10 how serious are you about getting X results?  
If we decide you are a fit \- will you be ready to move forward on the call? Or do you need someone else's approval?   
Bonus if you are getting qualified leads consistently \- enter the price range of your services.  
"Our services range from $1000-$5000. If we decide you are a fit for one of our packages \- will you be ready to move forward on the call? ..."

This is a very minimal landing page \- as discussed above \- you don't NEED one. But something barebones like this with some qualifying questions and social proof does well.

If you remember the DM script \- we are literally asking the same questions. We are helping them dive deeper into what they want and understanding that they need something to help them get there. It is OK to repeat these questions \- if not necessary.

Personally Reach Out

Once they have filled out your intake form \- email, call, or DM them.  
Ask them:

"Yo my friend\! I got your application for X. One more question for you \- what made you fill out the application? Where do you want to take this project?"

You can go on to ask more qualifying questions if you are iffy about them, but if you are just starting out \- get on calls and offer value to everyone.

When they respond, acknowledge their response and compliment them on wanting to change \- then tell them to schedule a call and drop your Calendly link.

Calendar With Additional Qualification

By now you should have your Calendly account setup. Create a specific "event" for your calls and title it "Strategy Call" (or discovery / clarity call... doesn't really matter what \- just don't call it a sales call.)

Questions For Your Calendar

Some of these may be repeat questions (which is important) but we want to dive deeper and see if they are actually a fit (financially and mentally).

In 90 days from now what results would you like to see in your \[fitness, business, relationships\]?  
Be honest... what is holding you back from getting there?  
If I can help you get X result, what would you want your \[fitness, business, relationship\] to look like after working with me? Paint me a picture.  
(Optional) The tiers of this \[service\] start at $X. Are you in the financial position to invest that into solving X problem right now?

These will give you a good idea if you need to reach out and just pitch from the DMs or accept the call.

If you have any questions related to this post \- drop them in the \#business-strategy channel\!

Enjoy the rest of your Tuesday my friends.

---

# The Outreach Formula For Consistently Landing Clients

We've talked about the longer / more time consuming method of outreach in the article How To Land $1k-$10k Clients In The DMs Without A Lot of Followers, but there comes a time when you can be more strategic (and less time consuming).

Here is how you craft the perfect outreach message. Whether it's DMs, cold email, or any other medium.

How To Structure An Outreach Message

Here is an example of what we want to accomplish. This isn't the BEST \- I think the first line could be a bit more personal and dive into my other content \- but this message got me on a call with her and I paid for her services ($3000/mo).

The Hook  
Dive into your prospect's content and find something that they would be proud of.

A deep tweet that didn't get much engagement  
An insight from a podcast episode  
A specific part of a blog post  
Any other post on social media that breaks their current content strategy (they may be testing something new and could use a compliment)

Then, let them know what you enjoyed about it or how it resonated with you.

Take a look at the first line from the screenshot above and make it better through deeper research.

Example: I wrote a blog post about focus a few months back. You could read that article and comment on one of the most complex parts and why you liked it (because I like to feel smart, and not many people saw it).  
3 Different Options For Authority

Social Proof And Name Dropping

EXACTLY how Shreya did in the screenshot above. Mention someone you have worked with (that the other prospect may know) and tell them the results you got them.

These results will make the other prospect want the same results.

Actionable Tips

Simple, give 2-3 ACTIONABLE tips that can help them immediately.  
This mainly works for freelancing services because you can SEE what they are currently doing. You can look through their landing page, copy, emails, or whatever else you specialize in.

This shouldn't be used for coaching offers UNTIL you know what they are struggling with.

Free Work

There are two ways to send free "work."

Offering to audit their current state  
Offering to send a "sample" of your work that they can use

For the audit: you are offering to give them 2-3 actionable tips on something that they've already done in video form. You can use Loom to record your screen and voice while doing this.

For the sample: Do what you are best at and send it to them for free (i.e. tweets, landing page, social posts, emails, copy, etc.)

THE KEY WITH THIS: only offer to send the free work. Don't send it at first. Simply ask, "Can I send you an audit/work I made for you? You can use it or trash it." Once they say "yes," THEN do the work and send them a link.

The Call To Action

The call to action needs to be plain and simple.

"Do you have time for a call this week to see if we can get you the same results?"

Or, "Do you have time for a call this week?"

Or however fits your natural voice.  
The Vessel

There are 3 ways to send these messages. I encourage you to try them all.  
If they don't respond via one channel, try another. Email them or DM them on Instagram/LinkedIn if they don't respond on Twitter.

The 3 Vessels:

Video DM \- write out your outreach message from above and record a video of yourself to send to them.  
Regular DM \- just send the DM and try different platforms.  
Cold email \- send your outreach message in the form of an email.

P.S. You can still follow the script in How To Land $1k-$10k Clients In The DMs Without A Lot of Followers \- and I encourage AT LEAST prequalifying a bit and having them tell you where they want to take their project (in terms of money and lifestyle).

I hope you enjoyed this article my friends \- please put this into practice and have a great Tuesday.

---

# Conversational Sales Script To Close $5k-$10k Deals

If you haven't already looked over the DM script for getting people on a call, check it out here.

I would also highly recommend using this script in conjunction with the Sales Training with Andy Strohm.

You’ve got your call scheduled, now it’s the time to seal the deal.

Your mindset going into this call should be focused on having a conversation with your potential client.

Putting yourself in a position of wanting to HELP them rather than sell them.

Trust me when I say this makes it much easier to bring the energy and flow through the call.

You can approach this call in one of two ways (I would try both and see which gives better results \+ is more enjoyable for you to do.)

1\. Offer free advice \- give them at least 3 URGENT and actionable steps they can take right now. At the end of giving advice, ask if they are confident in doing this by themselves. If they aren't, pitch your service. (This works well as a beginner to practice sales and get some easy consulting under their belt).

2\. Position your offer as help \- at the end, go straight into talking about your offer

Before we dive in… remember that this is a conversation. A hard-set script does not offer any flexibility.

Think of this as a framework rather than a script.

After EVERY question, acknowledge their answer and continue moving through the script.

1\. Say Hello

Say hello, talk about something like the difference in weather in the places you both live (or use another conversation starter). Simply have something that will start the call on a non-awkward note.

2\. Framing

You want to guide the conversation and remain in charge, setting expectations and telling them what will happen will keep you in charge.

You: “Okay so on this call I’ll begin by asking you some questions to gain a better understanding of your business and goals. Then, if it sounds like we would be a good fit, I’ll tell you a bit about myself and what I do. Then at the end, you can make a decision if you want to be a part of it. Sound fair?”  
They will say yes.

3\. Motivations

They hopped on the call with you for a reason. They are more than likely interested in your service, make them understand their interest more.

You: “So I always begin by figuring out people’s motivations. I talk to quite a few people and everybody has different reasons for talking with me. So.. why did you decide to take time out of your schedule to hop on this call with me today?”

4\. Understand Where They Are

Understanding where they are in terms of their goal will allow you to put yourself in the middle and help them reach their goal (while building trust). 

Having the prospect talk about it will make them realize that they may really need some outside help.

You: “So listen (CLIENT NAME) I know we don’t know each other very well just yet. I just want you to be honest about what you’re really struggling with right now. Like what’s the biggest problem that you’re facing right now in regards to (WHAT YOU HELP PEOPLE WITH)?”

This is where you want to dig DEEP. Here are some guiding questions to help them realize their deeeep pain.

These are just sample questions, you will get better at diving deep into their pain points with your own questions.

Can you tell me what you mean by that exactly? How else is that showing up for you?  
What has this cost you specifically? (time, energy, attention, money, peace of mind)  
What do you think is causing this to happen right now?  
How long have you been trying to solve this?  
Are other people affected by this? If so, who?

Here we are making them realize that their problem is not surface level.  
They are literally voicing their deep (and possibly biological) problem. This will help quite a bit.

P.S. DO NOT SKIP PAST THE EXTRA QUESTIONS. DO NOT JUST MOVE FORWARD AFTER ASKING WHAT THEY ARE STRUGGLING WITH.

You will get better at this over time.

5\. Where They Want To Be

Now that you have listened and understood their pain \- it is time to let THEM paint a picture of their own future for you.

This is where you can come in and become their savior.

You: "So tell me (NAME), where do you want to be in a year from now? Paint me a picture of your life. From your daily life to your business, what are you most looking forward to?

Let them talk without interruption. If they get stuck, give them suggestions... "Do you want to travel? How much do you want to make per month? How much time do you want to spend working? (Use questions related to your offer and what you can help them improve at.)

Now is the time to position yourself as the beacon of hope.

6\. The Beacon of Hope

When you are explaining your offer \- keep each part/section to a sentence or two and focus on the benefits (how it will help them reach their goal).

At the end of the day, all they care about is their own transformation and results.

Follow this structure:

"Based on what you shared today, It sounds like you are struggling with (insert problem) And you want to (insert goal/desire) but the thing that has been holding you back is (insert what is holding them back). Does that sound right?"

"Good news is, I can help you get there (without inconvenience). Are you confident in handling this on your own? Or would you like to hear a bit about what I do?"

"I have a 60-day program that would help you (insert outcome/goal they want)."

"Here is what you get \- (list the main parts of your offer along with the benefits, relate these benefits to the goals they gave you.)"

"This program was built specifically to help you solve (inset BIG problem) so that you can (insert BIG promise)."

"That way, you can have (insert big emotional benefits like more time with your wife, more energy, more money, etc.) and I will be walking you through it step by step. How does that sound?"

6\. Seal The Deal

At this time, they SHOULD ask what the price is. If they don’t, go ahead and tell them.

Give them a contrasting price & and price anchor if they pay ON THE CALL.

Contrasting price:

$5000 is nothing compared to the amount of time they’ve already wasted and will continue wasting trying to solve their problem.

You: “The investment today is $5000, which, would go towards solving \[X problem\] for life.”

“BUT, you seem like someone who would put this information into effect and get great results, those are the type of people I love working with. For that reason, I can knock off $1000 if you decide to move forward today, making the investment $4000.”

(This is optional, you will see why at the end.)

Now…. STAY QUIET

Do not start justifying your price if they take a bit to answer. The ball is in their field. Silence works.

If they say YES \- (prepare an invoice before the call) send the invoice and walk them through paying it. This is not as awkward as it seems.  
Once they pay, ask them when they would like to start and tell them what next steps are (normally this is onboarding.)

If they object \- most objections now will be about the price. Here are some ways to get around it.

The most common objection: "I will have to think about it"  
In this case, you either didn't qualify the prospect enough or they still have questions.

You: "If you don't mind me asking, why the hesitation? Is it related to the program? Or does it have to do with price?"

After they tell you, you can proceed accordingly with more info about the offer or proceed to downsell.

Some will try to negotiate and ask for more of a discount.

Have bonuses ready \- depending on your offer, instead of decreasing the price you can add on to the offer.

If it is 8 weeks of coaching, you can add on another 2 weeks of support or give them free access to some of your premium content.

If they do not accept this \- sell them on something else or take away parts of your offer.

(THIS is the importance of offer stacks / upsells and downsells)

If you are offering a landing page, email sequences, and Facebook ads for lead generation. You can take away the monthly retainer Facebook ads and upsell them after you deliver on the first offer.

If you are offering coaching \- you can create an "accelerated" version for half the price and a "micro" coaching offer to downsell further.

A lot of the time they won't want parts of it being taken away, they will accept the main price.

If they don’t budge, accept it and move on. There is nothing you can do about it and the client relationship would not work.

If you enjoyed this post, let me know by tagging me on Twitter and mentioning MMHQ with what you enjoyed about it and I'll retweet you.

Or leave a comment in \#General Chat\!
