# $5K Fast Track \- Stop Spinning Your Wheels & Focus On What Makes Money

Who is this post for?

Those that have a skill, information, or expertise that they want to sell via a digital product or freelance/coaching service.

Alright, the last thing I want is for people to be spinning their wheels and overthinking what they need to do to make money.

Refining your offer, marketing, and promotional tactics are great \- but if they take your focus away from lever-moving tasks, you won't get anywhere.

Your marketing can be the best in the business but if it isn't in front of people's faces then it is all in vain.

Where Do I Start?

For all of the beginners out there \- if absolutely nothing comes to mind when I ask you, "What do you want to sell?" Here's what you need to do:

1\) Learn SOMETHING, anything... even the information inside this community.

Interested in web design? Learn it.

Interested in mental performance? Learn it.

Interested in becoming a marketing consultant? Start studying what I'm teaching here and reach out to help people.

Email marketing? Learn.

Habits? Learn.

Twitter ghostwriting? Learn.

You cannot skip this phase.

Watch YouTube videos, buy courses, read blog articles, and do everything you can to become very well-read in that area.

2\) Learn by doing/teaching

You can only learn so much from YouTube and free information.

You need to build real-world projects (with skills) and get real-world results/experience (with interests/intangibles like habits)

THEN start reaching out to potential clients or create your first MVP (minimum viable product)

Some will say you aren't ready to do this yet, I think that's bullshit gatekeeping due to a large ego.

It is a necessary step to get SOMETHING out there so you can get direct feedback and make it better.

All of this should happen in a timeframe of 2-4 months.

If you fall into this category, pay close attention to the "personal development" side of things in this community and ask questions along the way.

Creating A Solid Offer The First Time Around

There is somebody out there that is making millions of dollars selling what you want to sell.

There's a dude making millions from teaching people how to take pictures of birds. BIRDS.

The point of this is, there is somebody that is already successful selling what you want to sell. You can research them, learn all about their offer, buy the product, and study their entire funnel.

Pay close attention to WHY it is a good offer.

What is the price? Why does that matter?  
What bonuses do they offer?  
How do they deliver the contents of the offer?  
What are the most compelling aspects of their copywriting?  
What is their guarantee?  
What pain points are they targeting? (Usually found at the start of their landing page)  
What is their quantifiable end result? (What specific solution are they solving?)  
WHO is their target audience? Why does that specific group of people need their offer?

How do you find these offers to study and emulate? From the people you learned from.

Or, just spend a day typing questions related to the offer in Google or find people that are selling similar in Facebook groups, on Twitter, or LinkedIn

This is only one aspect of market research (which you will continue to iterate on).

A few things to pay attention to here:

How do they position their offer in a way that makes people more money?  
How do they position their offer in a way that saves people more time?  
How do they position their offer in a way that solves a huge problem within the health / wealth / or relationships vertical?  
Do they offer one skill? Or a stack of skills to get results?

The thing that most people get stumped on is solving a problem BIG enough that makes the right person hand over their money without even reading into it.

Find the people that have already discovered that big problem, swipe it.

It's truly incredible how far ahead of the competition you can get just by doing this for a few days. (Yes, a few days if not weeks, spend time on this and write down everything you find.)

Okay... You Have An Offer. What Next?

A few things.

Testimonials  
SALES  
Traffic source

THESE are what you should be focusing on.

If you aren't at $5k/month then you should not be focusing on anything else but these.

Once you have a solid offer with solid testimonials that are pulling in money for you \- you can start to optimize, refine your marketing, build a more complex funnel, and pump money into growing your audience (so you can promote to more people).

Before we dive into those 3 things, let's talk about high ticket and low ticket offers.

If you want to sell a low ticket offer right out of the gate (digital product, physical product), that's cool. But understand that it will take some time to build a large enough audience to sell to if you don't have money to spend/test/and iterate with paid ads.

High ticket is the move, even if it's just one-off consulting calls to display your expertise, validate your offer, and pull in some early testimonials.

1\) Getting Testimonials and Getting Your Name Out There

For the time being, stop thinking about if you will get paid for your work or not. Lead with value, offer to help for free or at a discount, and ask for a testimonial in return.

How do you do this?

Take your offer, keep an eye out for your ideal customer on whatever platform you are on, and run through this DM script.

(P.S. In the next article, I'll talk about the best niches, angles, and positioning for Twitter)

DM them, offer them free help on a call (or in the DMs), write their name down in a word document, and set reminders to follow up with them for more help and a testimonial.

DMs are a lever-moving task.

Think of it as planting seeds. Every person you DM with the intention of helping, you gain experience, expertise, and possibly a loyal follower / fan for life.

Imagine if you sent 3 DMs a day for 2 months. If you didn't make $5k I would be baffled.

Go into this with the mindset of helping whoever you can.

2\) Sales Sales Sales

Now that you've started helping others, not only will you:

Feel more confident in your offer  
Validate your offer and refine it as necessary  
Possibly get offered money for your help

You will also:

Create the habit of DMing people (necessary)  
Understand that DMing random people is actually fun and rewarding  
Get used to putting yourself outside of your comfort zone

The MAIN thing that matters when you are starting out is sales.  
No fancy funnel or website.

All you need is either a gumroad page (for digital products) or a calendly with qualifying questions (to book sales calls from the DMs (post on this coming later))

If you do creative work, have a portfolio of course.

If you don't have a portfolio, create one by creating projects for people you would LOVE to work with. DM them and offer it to them for free. Do the BEST WORK POSSIBLE and even if they don't use it... you have a portfolio piece and possibly a testimonial.

Once you've help 3-4 people and have some form of testimonials, start reaching out for paid work.

Start off at $500-$1000 (for most marketing/creative skills).

If you offer something like graphic design, can you create a package that you can sell for this much rather than a one-off design?

I.E. a landing page, thumbnail, ebook cover, and ebook design for people that sell ebooks. Get creative with this.

Get better testimonials than before.

Increase to $1500-$2500.

Get better testimonials than before and focus on getting results.

Too many people try to do the bare minimum with this stuff.

Now, in terms of sales, there is a training dropping in a few days \- you'll be able to find it in the online business trainings. It's from Andy Strohm responsible for $70 million in sales.

He will walk you through the entire process and how to avoid common pitfalls when you are pitching your service.

A simple yet good metric: You have consistent calls with people.  
If you DM 3-5 people a day to start, get 1-4 on a call per week, and close 1 per week, that's a good amount of money.

Organic Traffic

We've touched a good amount on Twitter growth here.

If you sell high ticket (coaching/freelancing/consulting) then you don't need to build an audience... but it's fun and gives you perceived authority.

Plus if you ever want to switch down the road you can sell anything related to your interests along with your high ticket offer.

If you sell a low-ticket product, building an audience is almost implied or necessary. If you have money to spend, I would highly recommend investing in paid growth (retweets) and plugging your product under each one.

We can talk more about organic in another post, but understand that building an audience is extremely powerful and more than doable on Twitter.

Next Important Thing To Mention

Follow up, follow up, and follow up again.

Anyone that has done cold email knows this is where the real money is made.

If somebody doesn't respond after a day or two, send them a message like

"Hey, I know your DMs get busy and wanted to bump this up."

Follow up until you get a hard "no."  
Whew.. this was a long post and I hope I didn't miss anything.

If you have any questions, toss them in \#business-strategy.

If you enjoyed this post, leave a comment in \#General Chat.

If you really want to help out, tell me what you thought about it on Twitter and tag me in your post.

Have a great week everyone.

---

# The DM Seduction Method \- How To Land $1k-$10k Clients In The DMs Without A Lot of Followers

If you have ANY form of an audience (from 500-500,000) followers, you can make a boatload of cash. 

Before you do this \- your profile and content should reflect what you are offering.

Here is what you need:

1\. Somebody to DM

These are people that fit within your customer avatar. Considering many of you are doing this on Twitter \- make sure you are keeping an eye out for people that fit the bill.

In terms of inbound and outbound DMs \- you should be attracting the right people with The Twitter Matrix for content.

When you post social proof or authority tweets, you may receive a few inbound DMs (this is unlikely if you have a very small audience.

What you can do instead is DM 1-5 people every day that engage with your authority posts.

The best people to DM are the ones that retweet or reply, likes work as well but that would take a LOT of DMs.

2\. A high ticket offer (or any offer)

Coaching  
Freelancing  
Consulting  
Course

If you do not have an offer and are just starting out \- that's fine, you should be using these tactics as a way to give out free advice and validate your potential offer and get testimonials.

3\. An extremely simple funnel

Landing page (optional) \- To have social proof and other information before sending them to the questionnaire.  
Qualifying questionnaire \- to filter out qualified from unqualified before you spend time on a call with them.  
You can use your website software, Jotform, or Google forms for this  
Scheduling software (I.E. Calendly) \- to reach out to them after the questionnaire to get them on a call with you (an upcoming sales training with sales coach Andy Strohm will help you with the call).

THAT’S IT.

No crazy webinar funnels, no ads.

Your entire purpose with DM seduction is to hit some pain points, offer help, and have them schedule a strategy call with you.

It really is that simple.

Don’t think so? Read this:

My buddy Devin McDermott followed this system \- talked to someone with a porn addiction (most people) \- got him on a call and charged $375 per hour for coaching.

You don't HAVE to have an extremely high ticket offer to do this, but it is better to have multiple offers in place (an offer stack) so you can start high and work your way down for those that can't afford your full blown offer.

The DM Script

Below you will find a script to use to turn random people on the internet into a few thousand dollars (while also transforming their life for the better).

This script is not set in stone. You will have to use your judgment when going through this.

Don’t think of this as a script. Think of it as a 7 Step Framework. Seriously, use your own tone of voice with this. Talk like you are having a conversation over text.

Note: After EVERY SINGLE ONE of these messages \- if they do not respond within 24 hours, reply with a check-in message.

Example: “Hey \_\_\_\_\_\_, just wanted to bump this up. I’m interested in hearing about those goals.”

Some people won’t respond, this is why follow-ups are necessary.

The real money is made in the follow-ups.

Let’s dive in.

1\. Initial Message (Outbound)

Hey \_\_\_\_\_\_, I noticed you commented on my last post about \_\_\_\_\_\_. What was it that resonated with you?

This message can be anything really. Except for “hi,” don’t do that.

If they sent YOU a DM first, reply to their message and transition into the next steps.

Add Firepower To This Step:

Send a 1-2 minute video message talking directly to them  
Send a voice message if possible (unfortunately Twitter doesn't have this yet)

The more you can personalize this message \- the better.

2\. Transition

That’s awesome, I’m glad it could have an impact. I’m curious, what do you do for work? And what are you trying to achieve in (niche industry)?

Here we transition into a qualifying question and finding out where they want to be.

You should be able to tell if they can afford your services based on what they tell you from the first question.

The second question is to understand if you can actually help them accomplish something worthwhile.

3\. Details

(Comment on their work), how are those goals coming along?

They may answer this question early \- if that’s the case, move on to the next question.

4\. Roadblock

(Acknowledge what they said), what's holding you back from getting there quicker?

Make them realize they need help so you can position yourself as the solution.

5\. Visualize Their Transformation

(Acknowledge what they said), where are you looking to take this? Sounds like you have a big vision for this.

Again, we are showing them a possibility of a transformation and making them WANT it.

6\. Offer Help

(Acknowledge), I’ve helped quite a few people get (X results, plug a case study if you have one). I have a few suggestions that can help you get there. You open to take this connection offline and get on the phone soon?

If they say yes...

Awesome, I'll send you over a questionnaire so we don't have to waste a bunch of time on the phone.

7\. Send Questionnaire Link

Self-explanatory.

8\. Send Calendar Link To Qualified Prospects

Read through the questionnaire answers, ask the prospect more questions if you have to, and use your judgment on whether or not you actually want to take the call.

If you are new to this \- take as many calls as you can and just offer free advice. Give them actionable steps to fixing their situation. A few of them might even sign on with you \- or at least come back to you when they are ready.

Hope this helps for my fellow high ticket biz people.

---

# How To Create An Authentic Yet Compelling Bio

As some of you know, I'm notorious for changing my bio.

Well, I was... I haven't changed it in a while now that I've "figured it out."

But, I know people still struggle with crafting the perfect bio, and it makes sense as to why.

You feel like you have to:

Flex a crazy achievement to prove your authority  
Be as clear as possible so people understand what you do  
Fit every single thing imaginable into it (your topics, products, lead magnets, other links, and accomplishments)

With this post, I want to show you that all of this is as simple as being honest.

What Is Positioning?

Positioning is how you manipulate how your brand is perceived.

It is also how you manipulate your content, product, or copywriting of any sort – but we are here to talk about the top of funnel... how you position YOU and your brand.

It is the angle that people view you from.

It is the perspective that you plan to share with others, a perspective that they can follow along with.

So, let's just say that positioning is "perspective" in this case.

Now, what is a perspective composed of?

A goal that you are working towards – What broad goal are you trying to accomplish in your life? Financial freedom, mental clarity,

Where you are now and where you've been – What have you overcome in your life? How can you help others overcome those same things?

What you are doing to reach that goal – What are you learning? What are you building? How are those going to help others achieve that same goal? This is unique to you... others can have the same goal but a different way of getting there.

Take some time to answer all of those questions, as that will give you firepower to create a more authentic bio for yourself.

Let's run through an example:

My goal) Help other's reach their potential.

I understand the market and know this sounds a bit cheesy, so I don't explicitly say this.

Where I am / Where I've been) Tried every creative or marketable skill, failed at niche business models, and now use all of those skills as a personal brand.

What I'm doing to reach my goal) Studying philosophy, spirituality, and mastery while building a portfolio of digital products.

To make this even more simple and avoid sounding cheesy, here's a great bio template:

"I write about X, Y, and Z. Building: X"

Why does this work? Because it implies the goal that you are trying to achieve. It shows that you are a leader.

It is unique to you and you can avoid cheesy buzzwords relating to the broad goal you are trying to achieve.

Just Be Honest

Too many people overcomplicate this, so I want to show 2 great examples from Sahil Bloom & Justin Welsh.

Sahil has 722 THOUSAND followers with this as his bio, "exploring my curiosity and sharing what I learn along the way."

Is Sahil worried about his niche? Or is he worried about distilling the information that interests him and sharing it in an interesting way so he can attract interested people?

"Building a portfolio of one-person businesses to $5M in revenue."

That is Justin's goal.

Notice how he doesn't say "I built a one-person business to $5M in revenue."

Instead, he repositions the goal in a way that makes someone want to follow along.

People don't care what you're going to do, they care about what you are doing and what they can learn from you.

The point being, if you are a true leader, and actively pursuing a better life for yourself, all you have to do is be honest in your bio.

What are you studying? What are you building? How does it help others?

Answer those 3 questions and you'll have a trustworthy bio that brings in more followers than the dude flexing $100 billion dollar companies.

How This Transfers Over To Content

This does not only apply to your bio.

It applies to the content you are posting as well.

People always think, "I can't write about that, I don't have enough experience."

The thing is, you don't have to give actionable advice based on what YOU have done.

Instead, you can reposition from creation to curation and talk about something rather than at someone.

Instead of the headline:

"I've made $1 million in 30 days. Here's how you can do the same."

You can write:

"Alex Hormozi made $1 million in 30 days.

I reverse-engineered exactly how he did it.

Here's how I will use these principles to make $1M in 365 days:"

Simple, believable, and relatable.

You see what we did there?

We are curating content and advice in alignment with the goal that your brand is leading people toward.

That's all content is.

You can read, repurpose, and copy ideas if you want to.

When you apply them to what you are building and the goal you are trying to achieve, they become unique to you.

---

# How To Network, Grow, And Get Eyes On Your Content (Without Paying For Shares)

This process started as a Twitter thread, turned into a module in the Digital Economics cohort, then was used to help people get eyes on their writing in the my new course (2 Hour Writer).

I've seen people land jobs, have tweets go viral with little followers, and gain hundreds if not thousands of followers from doing this.

People usually fall into one of two camps:

Don't understand the sheer power and network effect of DMing people on a consistent basis  
Don't understand that you can get large accounts to share your posts (if you are strategic enough

DMs are how you network, grow, and get eyes on your content as a beginner (or whenever you want to get more traffic to your content).

But, most people suck at DMs.

Seriously. It's a problem.

Never, and I repeat never ever ever expect a response if all you send is:

Hi or hey  
How are you  
Can you follow me back  
A straight sales pitch with no prior connection  
A long block of text that takes too much time to read (especially if the sentences aren't spaced out)

You have to approach DMs tactically. Especially if you are reaching out to a big account that gets 10+ DMs an hour and probably doesn't check them (they usually skim over them to see if there is anything important).

Again, put yourself in the other person's shoes and think for a second. How can you stand out from the sea of crappy DMs that don't provide a shred of value before asking for something in return?

7 Steps To Non-Needy Networking

Knowing how to communicate and DM another person that you want to connect with will open up opportunities to paid work, social leverage, and meeting high-level people. You can use this strategy to:

Get a 50,000+ follower account to retweet your thread that will result in massive growth (the same goes for any other social platform sharing your post)  
Have connections that will share new growth strategies with you (Dickie Bush just sent me a LinkedIn tip the other day out of nowhere, I feel compelled to return the favor now)  
Join or create mastermind groups and begin forming your tribe (that you will grow with for much of your social media journey)  
To put your name in more peoples mouths. The more people that know about you, the more work and potential connections will be sent your way. Get your name in front of as many eyes as possible.

Here are the 7 steps of Non-Needy Networking:

1\) Find somebody that you WANT to DM

This is not exclusive to making connections. It is crucial for paid work as well.

The common theme among service businesses (like freelancers and agencies) is that their life is a living hell if they do not resonate with the client they are working with.

Reach out to people that:

You are inspired by  
You would want to work with  
You would want to strategize with  
You see potential for mutual benefit

When you are just starting out, you will have to work your way up the ladder. Start by DMing people that are within your follower range.

Once you have an audience and leverage, you can really reach out to anybody and get a warm response.

Where can you find people to DM?

The "following" list of accounts that you like

In the reply area of one of your mentors (if people are replying, it is implied that they are trying to grow and network)

Those are the main two areas to find people without using any fancy prospecting tools.

2\) Send them an inspired compliment

Find a piece of their content, work, or current projects that you are truly inspired by. Send it to them and tell them how it resonated with you.

This requires you to actually like their work

People love praise — and per the principle of reciprocity — will feel obligated to repay this soft favor.

An example for a tweet on managing emotions:

What's up Dan, this tweet hit me hard. I've been going through it the past couple of days and this instantly gave me some relief. Thank you. \[add the link to the post\]

Simple as that.

3\) Show interest in them

If they don't respond, you can try reaching out again in the same manner.

Showing interest is communication 101 — showing interest makes you interesting.

Ask them about:

Their goals  
What they are building  
What they do for work

This gives you the opportunity to give value (even if YOU don't have value to give right now).

Let's assume they respond with the generic "thank you so much."

Now, you can either find what they are working on from their profile or just ask them.

If you find what they are working on:

What are your next plans with Modern Mastery? It's been crazy seeing it grow, I'm curious what you've got in store.

If you can't find what they are working on:

Do you have anything that you're building right now? With that kind of content you must have something bigger in the works.

4\) Lead with value

This is the part that trips most people up.

Your first options are to:

See where you can help  
Send actionable tips  
Send resources, systems, or videos you've created or remember off the top of your head

Don't go straight for a transaction when you haven't given anything first.

If you have to ask more questions in order to send better actionable tips or resources, do it.

By resources I mean YouTube videos, articles, or anything that may be able to help them — or would pique their interest.

If you have no value to give you can:

Send a resource that can help them with their goals  
Connect them with someone else in your network  
Just continue having a good conversation and showing interest

Show that you are interested in helping them.

5\) Get on a call to make a deeper connection

This part is optional but recommended. You can skip straight to step 7 after a few days, but I would practice all of these steps at some point.

Making that "face-to-face" interaction is priceless. Nobody can see you, your personality, or your mannerisms via text.

When I was starting out, I was getting on zoom calls left and right with people that I wanted to get to know better. It's more normal than you think — and people are usually open to it when it is clear that you are just there to get to know them.

You can also take the conversation to somewhere like Telegram and send voice messages to make yourself seem more human. Most social accounts use Telegram and Whatsapp groups to communicate and strategize.

6\) Follow up with value

Remember their goals and keep an eye out for any content, resources, or people you can send their way. When you find something or someone, send it to them.

I remember you telling me about your plans for \[their project or goal\]. I found this today and thought you'd find it helpful.

"This" can be a YouTube video, article, lead magnet you found, or a person you connected with that may be able to help them.

7\) Follow up with an ask

By this point you've built a pretty damn solid connection. You've given value to the point where they are ready to return the favor. From here you can:

Ask them to join a mastermind group  
Send them one of your posts that you put a lot of time into  
Ask any specific questions you have for them without paying for consulting

If your plan is to leverage their audience for growth, be sure to write a post that they would want to share. Then, you can send it to them and mention that they inspired that post.

Yo, just wrote this up and thought you'd enjoy it. It was inspired by our previous conversation.

Do not ask them to retweet it. Let them engage with it however they see fit.

Even if you don't get a retweet or share, any engagement will help more people see it — helping you grow.

You should be reaching out to people almost every day. If you are immersing yourself in the environment of your interests, you should see inspirational people that you want to reach out to on a daily basis.

If you want to increase the chances of larger accounts responding to your DMs — follow them and engage with their content for a few days before reaching out so they are familiar with your face and profile picture.

A Few Words Of Advice

1\) If you plan on making an income or growing over the years as a creator, DMs are not optional.

You have to be consistent with meeting new people until you form a tribe that you can grow with (like I have with Joey and a few others.)

Aim for 5-10 DMs per day. Incorporate it into your engagement time blocks if that is something you are doing.

2\) If people aren't responding or sharing you, it's probably because your content isn't that good.

In that case, go through the Social Media Strategy category here, or check out The 2 Hour Writer for how to write with impact, my content ecosystem, and designing the lifestyle of a writer.

3\) This takes time, be patient.

Some people will see results after the first DM, some after their 30th.

There are subtle nuances to language and confidence that correct themselves with time. Everyone is at a different part of their journey, and if you are just starting yours, nothing will help you more than "putting in the reps."

Certain teachings won't resonate with you because your experience limits what you can perceive and interpret as useful.

---

# How To Capture Attention & 10X Your Engagement

People don’t remember what you say, they remember how you make them feel.

This is worth repeating:

Humans are emotional beings, not logical.

99% of the population have not developed themselves to the point of being free from — or in control of — their ego.

That is the foundation of capturing and holding attention.

Poking your reader’s ego.

Feeding it \= making them feel “good.”

Starving it \= making them feel “bad.”

If you can take people on an emotional journey of love, hate, excitement, deceit, calmness, and any other emotion that eventually ends in a benefit for their life — you have mastered the art of content creation.

Dan's 10 Koemmandments Of Capturing Attention

As you are scrolling through social media or just reading content in general — try to keep an eye out for these tactics being used. That is the best way to solidify this information in your head. Notice when your attention is being captured and question “why.”

There are many ways to capture attention. I’ve found these to be the most replicable and practical (number 8 is the most important):

1\) Specific Numbers

Using numbers in your hooks, headlines, or tweets will make people stop to see what the numbers relate to.

These can be in the form of:

Statistics — “There are 7 billion people on this earth”  
Dollar amounts — “Apples new $1175 iPhone has this new feature”  
Metrics — “I sent 322 cold emails” or “After 293 days…”  
Lists — “7 bad habits that are preventing you…”  
The more specific the number is, the more it catches peoples attention.

If you can’t make it super specific, that’s fine. Don’t stress it.

Here’s a recent example:

2\) Pattern Interrupts

A pattern interrupt is something that breaks people out of their normal conditioned patterns.

If someone is scrolling on Twitter and used to a lot of political commentary, a well formatted list tweet will make them stop their scroll.

Most of the things in this list are pattern interrupts.

3\) Negativity Bias

The human brain is wired to remember and pay attention to negativity.

This does not mean you have to be negative all the time.

It means you need to use the negative forms of words.

If you are saying something positive, but the point is better illustrated in its negative form, use that.

“You are going to achieve great things.”

Compared to:

“You will never hit rock bottom again.”

The second is most potent. We remember negativity. It is the most relatable aspect of many peoples’ lives.

It can still be a positive message while leveraging the reader’s negativity bias.

4\) Group Callout

This is simple, call out the specific person you are talking to.

If you are in your 20’s…  
Calling all creators, coaches, and freelancers\!  
Fathers are a gift to humankind…  
Even if your audience doesn’t fall into the specific group you are calling out, it will allow them to “pick a side” and compare themselves to what you are saying.

I talked about bodybuilders the other day. Even if people don’t consider themselves one, it helps paint a picture that they can relate to:

If someone talks about being a father, I can still relate because I will be a father one day. I will still pay attention to and take the advice.

This also works when it comes time to promote. You can call out exactly who the promotion is for and paint a picture of the problems they are struggling with.

5\) Problem Callout

Calling out the pains or problems people are experiencing will also make them relate to the post.

MOST people have encountered the same problem or pain as everyone else throughout their life.

If you can describe the feeling accurately, you have attention at your fingertips.

You don’t have to be dead on with this. Simply describing pain points will have people trying to relate their experiences to it. If they can relate, they will engage.

Here’s an example of calling out a pain as simple as “feeling terrible:”

6\) Potential Benefit

The opposite of calling out a problem. Again, pains and benefits. Your mind needs to think in pains and benefits. That is your unique “why” behind whatever “what” or “how” you are writing about.

7\) Social Proof

Again this is authoritative and implied an information gap.

When you flex your results or credentials, people automatically assume that you know more than them. They will take your content more seriously and read to find the information they are “missing.”

This works 100x better when it isn’t viewed as a “flex.”

Justin Welsh is the current king of this:

Use social proof to illustrate a point you are trying to make.

8\) Confidence & Conviction

This is by far the most important point here.

You can create highly impactful tweets with confidence alone — it allows other aspects of attention-grabbing to fall into place.

You are right about everything at this very point in time in relation to your goals, vision, beliefs, values, and everything else that forms your perspective of reality.

Your job is to have confidence and conviction in your beliefs and a credible or clear argument to back them up (if you have to).

Everyone is on social media to be told what to do in a confident way. Nobody is secure in their actions, choices, and beliefs. They are looking for someone to confirm them with confidence and give them that clarity to act.

Tools you can use to sound more confident:

Eliminate words that imply uncertainty  
Speak in absolutes when possible  
Exaggerate your point to add energy

Of course, do not abuse these for the sake of engagement.

Rather than saying:

“It may be wise if some people developed their skillset.”

Say:

“It is crucial that everyone on planet earth develops their skillset.”

Just by being confident, the words flow easier and the writing is more impactful.

I can go on to back that argument up with statistics or more creative firepower that I have in my mind.

Here is an example of me being confident in what I was saying:

This tweet got featured in a big newsletter and sparked a lot of controversy.

People were arguing whether or not it was the “greatest” skill. Some were proposing what their greatest skill was.

This made people comment and quote tweet, leading to more engagement and impressions.

I wrote this tweet in the moment when I had executed on an idea quickly. Doing that gave me a lot of joy, so I wanted to share that joy with others. It worked.

Is it 100% correct? No.

Was it 100% correct when I wrote it, through my perspective, relating to my personal experience?

Yes. At the time I was 100% convinced that that was the greatest skill.

I went on to add nuance in the replies. If I had added nuance in the actual tweet, it wouldn’t have done as well and opened up the opportunity to be featured in a big newsletter.

The people YOU want to attract aren’t the people that “hate” on your work.

Here is one other — a bit more extreme — example. Can you sense the motivational and practical energy “flowing through the screen?”

By the way, these types of high-energy advice posts pull in quite a bit of followers.

In summary — have some conviction behind what you are saying. This is not a skill that needs to be trained. It’s just a matter of writing the words in the most impactful way. Leaders don’t dance around the point they are trying to get across.

9\) Active Voice

Active voice implies that there is a story. It eases people into what you are saying.

Passive voice is often boring and gives away the “mini-story” too early. There is no anticipation that makes people want to figure out what happened next.

When you are practicing writing tweets, go through this article and edit out any passive voice you are using.

This also helps with being perceived as confident.

10\) Warnings & Cautionary Advice

What should people look out for when they are trying to achieve something?

Can you warn them of something they will encounter as they are trying to reach where you are now?

When you are doing your weekly reflection, or just reflecting on your life, what roadblocks can you help people navigate?

This is best illustrated with this tweet. I hit on a hot topic like dopamine and warned them of another hot topic (then wrapped it up with confidence).

This sparked a LOT of controversy, but I have research to back up that point AND gave nuance in the replies to build a deeper connection with my audience:

# The Viral Content Repurposing Machine

I don't know why I hadn't made this connection before, so with this post I want to give you a simple, actionable, and highly effective strategy for social growth on all platforms.

We should all understand content repurposing at this point — but there is a foolproof way of going about it.

We will talk about

Generating ideas that have already done well and have viral potential  
Structuring a list-style post that can be guaged for engagement  
How to post that list on all other platforms  
Turning the list into a viral thread  
Using the thread as a carousel or YouTube video

In this case, Twitter is our "virality tester" — you will understand soon.

And before we start — this can easily turn cheesy and hurt your account. Be mindful of the Social Matrix and mix it up between purely growth and authority posts.

Viral Idea Generation  
We've talked about this before in this post. Here's a brief overview:

The internet has already vetted ideas for us. We can have a rough estimate of what content will do well by what has already done well – or what is currently doing well. This means looking for

YouTube videos that have a lot of views (or are in your favorite creators videos sorted by popularity)  
Medium articles that show up on your homepage based off of your interest  
Top articles that show up when you search for your topic on Google (example: type "best habits" into Google)  
Top tweets from creators in your niche  
You can type "from:thedankoe min\_faves:500" in the twitter search bar to find tweets of mine that have gotten over 500 likes. You can do this for any creator, just replace the handle after "from:"  
I use TweetHunter both for ideas and to schedule my content with ease  
Pinterest, Instagram, TikTok \- I have not figured out how to find the best posts, but if they get high engagement you can take them

Now, we have an idea for a post — preferably one that aligns with your Content Pyramid and/or a section from your product/service if you plan to sell at the end.

Write A List Style Tweet  
Like this:

This is a poor example... for a reason. Anyone can write a "7 things I wish I knew as an 18-year-old" list (and that will always do well). 

But really anything can be turned into a list, like the above pic. That would eventually turn into a thread like, "The 3 reasons modern humans are unhappy:" (This could be tweaked to do better of course).

Why a list-style tweet?

It gives people multiple options to "agree" with one of your points, making it more likely for them to engage  
It acts as a pattern break on consumer's timelines because they follow their friends as well, who would never write a list tweet  
Humans love lists. They are more likely to read bullet points over anything else.  
They are the main style of content I wrote when I was a beginner and led to the most growth.  
Since it is just a tweet, you can use it as a test to see how much engagement a thread (or other posts) would get

Posting To Other Platforms  
This part is simple, you can:

Screenshot, edit, and post the screenshot of the tweet to platforms like Instagram, LinkedIn, etc.  
Create a reel, TikTok, or YouTube short according to what will work for the platform

Here's an example of a post that has always been going viral on TikTok. When you pair it with viral sounds, you are pretty much guaranteed growth.

And here's an example of posting on Instagram (if you include the likes and retweets in the image, it acts as social proof that gets people to engage. The idea is already validated to them)

Then, if you wanted, you could post that to LinkedIn, or just rewrite the Tweet on there.

Turn The List Into A Viral Thread  
I'm sure you've all seen what is doing well lately on Twitter. Dakota as an example has been killing it with these threads (he has been somewhat of a trendsetter in this regard).

Others are copying him and following his lead quick.

The easiest way to stand out and not be lumped into the bunch of copycats is to just change the hook or headline according to The Ultimate Thread Writing Guide.

I'm sure you can see how the list tweets make this process simple.

Post the list tweet  
Use the points as subtopics in the thread  
Expand on those points in 1-2 tweets in the thread  
Add a call to action to subscribe to your newsletter at the end

This is what all of the big accounts do. They don't sell on the timeline. They plug their newsletter and sell through there. You can sell on autopilot if you've gone through the Email Marketing Roadmap.

Repurpose The Viral Thread

Since these are so easy and streamlined to write (you already have the outline, it should take \~20 minutes to expand on each point into a thread), you can write 2-3 of these threads a week.

THEN, you can gauge engagement again, choose the one that did best, and post it as a carousel to Instagram or as a YouTube video.

Since these posts almost always do well on all platforms (because they are an evergreen content style), you will grow on YouTube. We will discuss why you aren't growing on other platforms in a bit.  
The Daily Process  
I would incorporate all of this into your content creation routine. It is simple and nearly automatic.

Remember, we are generating ideas from content that has already done well on other platforms. The idea is already validated and will do well IF you are getting eyes on it.

1\) Post a list-style tweet once a day.

This will result in growth on it's own, and has many other benefits for creativity and the mind.

Give it a day and gauge what it's engagement is. I wouldn't pay too much attention to this if you are a smaller account because engagement is inconsistent.

You can either store these tweets in a collection in TweetHunter or somewhere of your liking.

2\) Post something to Instagram, TikTok, or LinkedIn

According to whatever post did the best, use that as inspiration for a post on another platform. These do not all have to be list tweets.

3\) Give it a day or two, then turn it into a thread

Again, simple. Craft a good hook, expand on each point of the list tweet, and add a CTA to your newsletter or whatever you sell.

4\) Turn the thread into an Instagram carousel, LinkedIn article, Medium article, or YouTube script

Easy peasy and should take no longer than 3-4 hours a week for viral content that results in growth and sales.

Start Viewing Business As A Game  
Before we end, I want you to start viewing this as a game.

I see so many people destroying all chances of their growth because they let their ego get in the way.

"I'm too good for posting simple and actionable content"

 Don't complain when you aren't growing. It's not the algorithm, it's you.  
Understand that you probably read that basic content when you were starting out and wouldn't be here without it  
Understand that Twitter is top of funnel. The majority of your content is going to target the lower levels of awareness. Especially if your content topics are rather broad

See engagement, followers, and authority as a game.

How can you craft a tweet that will result in all of the above?

Getting Eyes On Your Profile  
If you aren't getting any traction on these posts:

You are just starting out and don't have any followers  
You aren't playing the game. You don't have a network you can send these to boost exposure and leverage other peoples audiences (the only other way to grow aside from commenting on everyone's posts, but that is time draining and demotivating. Just make friends and help each other grow)  
You are afraid to pay for retweets, story shares, or other types of paid growth that all of the big guys do. If I have an offer that sells, why would I not invest $500 to get my post exposed to 100,000 more people? The growth should pay for itself 5 times over.  
You aren't saying anything controversial, polarizing, or you aren't confident in the way you are writing it. Give people a reason to click on your profile.  
That's it\!

If you bake this into your content strategy I am confident you will see faster growth and newsletter opt-ins.

If you have any questions regarding this, post it in the Business Strategy or Writing and Idea Generation channel\!

---

# Evergreen VS Meta Growth Content

By now we have a solid understanding of what we should be posting on social media. We need to maintain an authoritative & authentic brand while still growing. If you are unaware of what I am talking about, read about the Social Matrix here.

When people neglect growth content, they either don't make it off the ground and quit — or they stall and remain around the same follower account for months (until they recognize its importance).

This is something I see all too often across all social media. It is a spiritual game. A matter of awareness. If you are not tweeting to the 90% of people that have a low level of awareness, how can you expect to grow quickly?

This is an ego problem for most, as they "don't want those type of people following them." Again... awareness. Your job is to raise their awareness / consciousness (through your funnel) to a point of being highly educated on a specific topic (that you teach).

Short-form social media platforms (Twitter, Instagram, TikTok, YT shorts) do not allow depth. People are not on those platforms for depth. You have to play to the algorithm for the sake of filling your funnel to educate people and bring them to your level.

Ok... that was a bit long of an intro — but growth content is IMPORTANT. Especially as a beginner. Play the game until it becomes an art. In other words, do what you have to do until you can do whatever you want.

Evergreen Growth Content

There are a few content styles that have been on social media and blog platforms for the entirety of internet life. They are almost always a safe bet to emulate and schedule in your weekly / monthly content.

When I talk about evergreen content, I am including both the SEO definition and my own. SEO evergreen content means that it is relevant and will continue to garner traffic (blogs and YouTube have this). For other platforms like Twitter, evergreen content can be posted again and again from a different perspective to keep growth coming in. This is where TweetHunter thrives, as it teaches you how to write this content \+ gives you ideas and inspiration.

Evergreen content includes:

Listicles  
Quotes or "insights"  
"I tried XYZ and this happened"  
Personal stories  
Questions  
How to for beginners

Now, these all have specific ways that perform best on any given platform.

I've made a collection of some of my evergreen content-style tweets here so you can see how they would be posted.

The only ones that I didn't include where the "I tried" and "Quotes" style. But I could easily post a "After a week of daily beef liver, I got these benefits..." or quote my favorite author with "Alan Watts famously said..." and those would do well while bringing in some followers.

I would say that this is fairly apparent on most platforms. You understand what a listicle blog of YouTube video is. "7 Ways To Boost Your Confidence" and the rest. Now that you understand this, you will catch onto these trends more often.

You can see this done on Instagram as well. Carnivore Aurelius does list style posts and carousels very well. There are huge inspirational pages that do quote style posts well. And of course there are niche accounts that have a ton of "How to for beginners" style content.

Again, all of these are great for growth and should take up the majority of your content, but you need authority and authenticity style content as well. Especially if you are a personal brand and / or plan to monetize.

Since I've started on TikTok, I've noticed that these evergreen content styles are still on the platform, just posted in a way that favors TikTok style content. Can you tell what a listicle style post looks like on Twitter by looking at my TikTok? (Not the ones with my tweets pasted on a bg video).

The lesson of all of this that many people miss: YOU HAVE TO POST EVERGREEN GROWTH CONTENT. ESPECIALLY AS A BEGINNER. Stop trying to post like a 100K follower account that can get engagement on everything.

Meta Growth Content

TikTok made me very aware of current "metas" on social media. Jak Piggot is a prime example of milking a specific content style that does well and growing like crazy. I am emulating him and have grown to 4K in a week thanks to Jimmy Farley's TikTok course.

From what I've seen, the content that is favored to most is a crossover between evergreen content and HOW it is posted on the platform.

"I Tried X For Y Days" is going crazy on YouTube right now.

Long-form listicles are going crazy on Medium and Twitter right now \- Millenial Money Woman is a prime example with her threads.

TikTok has it's own trends (obvious) that go crazy all the time.

And Instagram... I'm honestly not sure. There algorithm is all over the place and I can't seem to figure it out lol.

There is no way of knowing what the current meta will be. All you can do is keep an eye on social media and see what starts to do well. Create your own swipe file and write content that emulates certain styles that start to do well.

If you have any questions regarding evergreen or meta content, feel free to pop them in the Lounge\!

I have some incredible posts lined up over the coming weeks. I will be continuing the product build to 6 figures and posting my current TikTok strategy just because it has so much potential to drive traffic.

---

# How To Tell A Joke (And 10X The Impact Of Your Writing)

The other day I watched a YouTube video that broke down the joke writing process. This brought to light some of my "unconscious competence" when it comes to writing tweets (or other content).

I wanted to share it with you all — as this will serve as a primer for a content writing live session that we will have soon.

This process has birthed some of my best Tweets.

The only difference between a good joke and impactful content is the degree of seriousness.

Before we start:

I have a feeling that many people starting out on Twitter (or any other platform) thinks that writing short-form content is quick and easy. It CAN be, but not at first.

When I was at 300 followers or so I would lay in my bed at midnight staring at my screen trying to think of a tweet idea. I would refine it to perfection and would not go to sleep unless I had content scheduled.

If you eliminate the expectation of it being "easy" at first, you will build a writing habit and it will become second nature over time. You have to put in the reps and time to get better at this.

The Joke Writing Process  
When comics are writing a joke, there are a few crucial steps.

Step 1\) Just Start Writing.

Seriously, just start. Write down one word. One topic. Write down a series of words. Write down a sentence that pops into your head.

You need SOMETHING written in order to get ideas flowing in the direction of that word. The act of writing down ONE word/sentence gives you something to iterate on.

Once you have something written, finish the thought and write anything else that may come to mind.

Personal experiences  
Feelings associated with the topic  
Pains or benefits associated with the topic  
Answer the question: "What's in it for me?" (the reader)  
Brainstorm the "how" and "why" behind the topic you wrote down  
Etc

By now, you should have a sentence or two. It may be coherent, it may not be. That's okay.

If you need help with inspiration or idea generation, I use TweetHunter (as do most of the people that write good content).

Step 2\) Create A Setup

In content, this is known as the hook. In a story, this is the setting — or giving context to what you are going to say.

Standup comedians need to set up the context before the punchline, or else the joke will flop.

Storytellers need to paint a picture of the scene, or else you won't be able to follow the story. There will be a lack of depth.

How can you frame the topic in an interesting way?  
How can you grab people's attention and spark curiosity for what's next?  
What is a problem / experience that people go through related to the topic?  
What is the big idea that you are trying to get across?  
Do you have a story / experience that you can set the scene for?

Again, you can use something like TweetHunter for good hook inspiration, or you can scroll through Twitter, YouTube, Medium, or Instagram (EVERYTHING you see is a hook, some good some bad).

Step 3\) Get Specific

This is where true virality, laughs, and relatable stories happen — by getting specific.

What are the steps to achieving/relieving the benefit/pain?  
Can you use a metaphor to help explain your point? Here is a viral tweet of mine that uses a metaphor — and another one here  
Can you use numbers or percentages? This helps capture attention  
From your personal experiences — can you describe emotions, feelings, or actions with depth?

Specificity is all about relating to the reader and making them understand what you are trying to put across.

Here's what is going through the reader's mind as they are scrolling:

"Oh wow, this is so me"  
"Damn, that hits deep"  
"I believe the same thing, thanks for the confirmation"  
"I agree with this" (think of the like and RT button as "I agree")

They aren't saying that exactly, but those are helpful for guaging the potential impact of your idea.

Another thing you can think about: would YOU like, retweet, and click on the user's profile if you saw the tweet on your timeline.

Step 4\) Use Your Favorite Framework / Template

This part is optional, but effective. There are dozens if not hundreds of ways to structure a story, sales copy, or anything else that grabs and holds attention.

AIDA (attention, interest, desire, action)  
Headline, lead, body, conclusion  
Listicles ("the top 7 habits of 2022")  
One liner tweets  
Anything you can find in TweetHunters dashboard or resources

Many people START with this part, but it becomes 10x easier when you already have the idea fleshed out.

After you have a completed idea, you can then turn it into 3-5 different variations with the SCAMPER technique. You can learn more about that at the top of my master swipe file.

Writing A Tweet With This Process

Start:

The most effective thing you can do

Then (inspired by a previous tweet of mine):

The most effective thing you can do is block off 1 hour a day dedicated to the person you want to become

Idea that sparked after writing that: think of it as going on a date with yourself

Revised:

The most powerful thing you can do is set aside 1 hour a day for you and the person you want to become

Create a setup and get a bit more specific:

Set aside 1 hour a day for the 2 most important people in your life.

1\) You  
2\) The person you want to become

Specificity is there, punchline is there (but could be stronger):

Set aside 1 hour a day for the 2 most important people in your life:

No distractions, no phone, just you and the person you want to become.

Boom. There is a solid, specific setup and a semi relatable punchline. It has numbers, I don't give everything away upfront, and it makes people stop and think for a bit. It's also very easy to apply the advice.

I scheduled this tweet for tomorrow. If you want to see how it did, you can copy and paste this into the Twitter search bar:

from:thedankoe "Set aside 1 hour a day for the 2 most important"

I could EASILY turn that into 3-5 different variations and even a thread.

That's it for this post, we have a live content writing session on Wednesday — if you are reading this later, you will be able to find it in the Trainings tab.

If you have any questions relating to this post, pop em in the Lounge\!

---

# How I Made $3000 Per Month With 300 Followers On Twitter (With Digital Products)

The start of my Twitter journey was different from most. I had a background in marketing, was studying advertising, and understood my customer avatar (myself).

I bought my first Twitter growth guide without meaning to start a Twitter account... I was just a lurker at the time. I saw the opportunity and said "f\*ck it, why not."

My account started off with 110 or so followers, friends and family. I branded myself as the web design and mindset guy. The thing is, I didn't want to do it unless I was making a decent amount of money upfront. I had money coming in from freelancing, so this would just be the cherry on top. (This was before I realized the true power of Twitter, it's changed the direction of the business for good).

This is the earliest screenshot I have of my account, the timestamp is March 2020:

This is my Gumroad dashboard for January 2020:

I started my account in November 2019 \- so I'm estimating I was a bit above 300 followers.

This can also give you an example of compound growth. It took a bit to break 500, 1000, and 2000 followers. Although there are better ways of going about it then I did \- like how JK Molina outlines in this training.

Also...

This is excluding my freelance income (which also increased with Twitter). There are a multitude of trainings and articles on sales and prospecting on Twitter in here.

Double also...

This can be done with any product. There is no need to overcomplicate this process. If somebody else is selling a product that you have expertise in, you can sell your own version. (This is the best way to go about it).

Step 1\) Creating The Digital Product

My goal was to teach developers how to freelance with their web development knowledge.

I had bought many freelancing and web design courses in the past, so I knew it would sell. The idea was validated.

I could have been an affiliate for any one of them, but I figured I might as well make my own (since I had results and a different perspective) and take 100% of the profits.

Here's what I did to create the product in under a month:

Created a rough outline of the chapters I wanted in there  
Went back through the courses I previously took to fill in the gaps  
(Keep in mind this was for inspiration only, to make sure I was covering all bases in terms of topics I taught)  
Wrote the ebook during my focused work blocks (it ended up being \~100 pages double spaced)  
Brainstormed a title, subtitle, and cover image  
Went through the course landing pages that I had taken before, wrote down the benefits and pain points I could use for my own landing page  
Uploaded everything to Gumroad (no prelaunch or anything)  
Started promoting (more on this later)  
Built out my welcome and sales sequence for this product so I could sell on autopilot (Email Marketing Roadmap)

If I had taken my time to market it correctly (via the Advanced Marketing Roadmap), I probably would have made much more, but I just went with it.

Step 2\) Getting Traffic To The Offer

This is where many people go wrong... they want to make money without spending money. I wanted to grow a digital asset and sell my product, so I cut back my spending and started investing $500/month into my growth.

YOU NEED SEMI INTERESTED TRAFFIC (AND A GOOD OFFER) TO SELL YOUR PRODUCTS.

You cannot get these results at 300 followers if you are not willing to invest in paid traffic. (In this case, paid traffic \= retweets).

I paid a big account that was already selling a web design product for 30 retweets. I figured if they were teaching people web design, I could teach them to freelance with that skill (eventually I went on to create my own web design product because it paired well with the freelance product).

I would send the account my tweets daily, they would retweet, I would gain followers and profile visits, and I would promote the product accordingly.

(I also had the link and a call to action in my bio \- because I knew that many would look at my profile without following me... this got more sales than you would think)

It was that simple.

Create decent content  
Give actionable advice according to the product you are selling  
Promote the product  
Get eyeballs on your profile (free \= slow, paid \= fast, nothing wrong with either)

You are selling and growing at the same time.

Step 3\) Networking & Getting Affiliates

This happened by luck, but down the road (when I was closer to 1000 followers) I was trying to network with developer accounts.

I tried offering to pay one of the accounts, he was at 16K followers at the time and declined because he didn't think his retweets were worth the money.

Time went on and he realized that I was selling a freelancing product. He said, "oh man people ask me all the time how to freelance" so I offered to make him an affiliate.

He started promoting my product, bringing in an extra $1500 rev or so a month.

After my product had decent reviews and traction, I started looking for other affiliates.

Step 4\) Creating Complimentary Products and Iterating

After some time, I realized I didn't want to be the web design guy, so I started to pivot in how I was selling my products.

First, I created a web design product (Websites That Work) and launched that. I sold that for a bit as a standalone product.

Eventually, I combined the 2 into the "Modern Money Bundle" and started to target those that wanted to learn a skill and learn to sell it.

This extended the "shelf life" of these products. I was able to continue pulling in consistent revenue because I tested different angles and created new offers out of things that were already made.

Once I hit 10K followers, I created my Twitter course. Sold that on its own for a bit, then added it to the Modern Money Bundle.

Those sold for a bit longer, and are all now in the One-Person Business Roadmaps.

I hope you are all starting to see how this is a long-term game of persistence and iteration.

If you have any questions about my journey or how I can help with yours \- pop a question in the \#business-strategy channel\!

Happy Wednesday my friends.

---

# The Content Pyramid For Unlimited Ideas

I've gotten a lot of questions about The Content Pyramid lately, and when I think back to the first Twitter course I bought — mapping out my content pillars and ideas was the first thing I did.

If you are struggling with idea generation for content, this article is for you.

Let's start with these questions:

What are you good at?

What can you talk to your friends for hours about?

What do you want to learn more about that will make you (and those around you) a better person?

This is what you will be creating content about, and preferably helping others accomplish in exchange for money.

Following The Content Pyramid will give you unlimited ideas for tweets (and all other social posts and videos).

Pillars

Most personal brands, creators, coaches, or freelancers on social media have 2-5 content pillars. These are usually sub-markets.  
For clarification, the main markets are:

Health  
Wealth  
Relationships

Sub-markets are branches off of those:

Health   
Exercise  
Nutrition  
Mental health  
Wealth   
Business  
Investing  
Money management  
Relationships   
Dating  
Marriage  
Friendship

What are the sub-markets that you have the most experience in and want to pursue?

Don't overthink this too much \- it doesn't really matter if it's classified as a sub-market or not. What matters is that you have a broad market to work down from for relevant content ideas.

Topics

Think of topics as something you discuss with your friends for a few minutes \- or what you see in a YouTube video.

Topics are things that you can write a blog post on, create a video on, or just discuss (works for threads too).

On Twitter \- you don't really Tweet about topics as there is too much to fit into the 280 character count.

We need to write down topics for the sake of creating content.  
Examples for bodybuilding:

Weight training  
Gaining muscle  
Cutting

Examples for business:

Audience building  
Freelancing  
Marketing

You get the point \- and you can probably see the connections with "niching down" with everything related to marketing that we've talked about here.

Content

You can see where we are going with this... now we break them further into content ideas.

These can be used in many ways:

Blog posts  
YouTube videos  
Tweets/threads  
Instagram posts/carousels

Pretty much the same thing as Topics, but a tad more refined.

The Secret Sauce

Now we need to turn these content ideas into high-engaging posts.

I've been using Tweet Hunter as the start of all of my content creation. You can plug any of your content pillars, topics, or favorite accounts and study all of their best tweets. A tweet that does well is then turned into more content across all social media channels.

The BEST posts are relatable.

How do we make these pillars/topics/content relatable in a short and punchy way?

By understanding the benefits that they provide and the problems they solve.

Humans are emotional and selfish creatures... if something can help them, they will listen. If you pinpoint the problem they are having, they will listen.  
You can dive deeper into your target audience's problems by reading up on market research here.

What was your former mindset on the problem?  
Why did you implement the advice?  
What results were you hoping to get?  
What problem of yours were you trying to solve?  
What did you struggle with?  
What were your biggest “aha” moments?  
What were your objections?  
What did you struggle with the most?  
What do you wish you had done differently?  
What are you going to do to prevent that problem from happening again?

Ideas For Unlimited Content Creation

Per The Content Pyramid \- all of your tweets, in essence, are just words that dance around your reader's emotions. They should always have a heavy focus on:

Transformations   
Where they are now \- how it feels to be there, common experiences  
Where they want to be \- how it feels to be there, why its better than where they are now  
Exaggeration   
Make the deep pain points sound painful  
Use absolutes   
Never, always, best, worst \- no middle ground  
Stand firm in your beliefs (but be open enough to change them if you are proven wrong)  
Think about how the problem affects them from a health, wealth, or relationship standpoint.   
Building a business allows people to work from anywhere, from their laptop, and do what they want with their time (benefits). It also allows them to avoid wage slavery, fire their shitty boss, and escape the life-sucking cubicle (exaggerated pain points).  
Exaggerated pain points and benefits are key for one-liner tweets or at the end of a longer tweet to tie everything together.

Start looking for this in good tweets you see. Start forming the mental connections about what makes a tweet do well.

Good Headlines Make For Good Tweets

If a blog post is doing very well \- that usually means it will do very well on Twitter (this works for YouTube as well, not just blogs).  
One-off headlines are great for short tweets.

Example: If you want your content to stand out, learn how to break the rules.  
I just found that on Medium. I could tweet it out right now and probably get 300+ likes. (Remember to not just copy things word for word \- FOCUS ON THE IDEA YOU ARE TRYING TO CONVEY BEHIND THE TWEET. Be clear about it.)

Headlines make for great tweet topics.

Example: 9 signs a person is really happy with their life.  
That is the first line of your tweet, then list out the 9 things.  
These 9 points can also be turned into individual tweets.

Once you get the hang of high-performing tweet structures, these will start to write themselves naturally.

Find a huge community blog like Medium, Lifehacker, or one in your niche. Bloggers will usually post their own articles to these platforms \- pay attention to the ones that do well and use the headlines/content tactically.

Idea Generation Tactics

One of my favorite times of the day is my "Idea Generation Session." In other words, an intentional learning period where I:

Read articles on Medium or elsewhere related to my target audience and content pillars.  
Watch YouTube videos of the same.  
Read books or listen to audiobooks pertaining to my own interests or my audiences.

Keep a notepad, journal, or notetaking app next to you to jot down any idea that comes to your mind.

In short \- set aside time for consuming content that already does well.

Another great way to do this \- that we already touched on \- is creating a 'list' on Twitter of the accounts you aspire to be like, write like, and impact like. Spend some time reading over their tweets to keep their writing style fresh in your mind.

Again, I'd like to give a special mention to Tweet Hunter for doing this all for you. (this is the first step in my creative process).

This is a great way to "force" yourself to have relaxation time. It calms your mind and starts to make you think for yourself again. Twitter is notorious for polarizing views. Most other content is not.

Creating A Swipe File

Whenever a tweet passes by your eyes that makes you think, "Damn, I wish I wrote that," DO NOT let it just pass by. Copy and paste it somewhere safe (like Notion) so you can refer back to it when you need inspiration.

You can duplicate and study my swipe file here.

# The Evolution Of Your Content, Ideas, & Brand

I've seen way too many people getting discouraged lately that they aren't "on par" with bigger creators and brands. This is natural, it happened to me, so I want to break down my experience in the evolution of my brand — and the things you should focus on as you grow.

Your content, bio, message, and overall branding will be different at 100 followers than it will at 1,000 \- 10,000 \- and 100,000. You will refine your message, move away from "what works," and start creating ideas that can be tied to you.

This is the journey to exponential growth and authority.

(By no means is my journey perfect, but I will speak from my experience and what I have noticed working for others).  
Under 10,000 Followers

This is arguably the most difficult part of the journey. You are testing what kind of content you like writing rather than what content works (because you don't have an audience for feedback).

The best thing you can do is to emulate bigger brands. See what is working for them but understand that they already have leverage. Naval can have nothing in his bio. If you did that you would just look like an anon account.

The secret to this is crafting your bio as if you were a 10,000 follower account. People should think, "Wow I've found a little known gem\!"

Your Profile

1\) It needs to clearly state what you help people do.

You need to answer their question... "What's in it for me?"

You need to focus on the benefits of what you teach. If you talk about personal growth \- what are the tangible benefits of that? (That they actually care about?)

A great way to get this across is with this template. You don't have to use it word for word, but it will help you structure what you are trying to say:

Learn to ABC so you can XYZ

Or

Lessons on ABC so you can XYZ \- Tweets on ABC so you can XYZ

Example: Tweets on personal growth and holistic health so you can live stress free.

Simple as that.

There are more examples in this article on profile optimization.

2\) You should have a link to SOMETHING

People want to follow leaders. That's why they are called followers.

Leaders speak confidently and are open to feedback. (Confidence in your tweets is an engagement hack. People can sense it.)

Leaders provide value. They teach. They have some form of a resource for someone to download or buy. If you are afraid of selling, this is even more reason to do it. So you can get over that fear.

Start an email list (even if you aren't going to write emails yet.) Write a free guide. Create a product. Have a questionnaire to schedule a call with you. Anything. Show that you can give them something worth their time.

Consumers follow producers. So produce something deeper than surface level engageable content. Give them something MORE.

3\) Your pinned tweet should show some form of authority, social proof, or authenticity... again, "What's in it for me?\!?\!"

If you haven't watched the JK Molina training yet, watch it here. He breaks down how to grow to 2,000 followers the fastest way.

You should have either:  
A tweet about your story / transformation  
A tweet that has a lot of likes (social proof)  
A tweet that gives away so much good information people can't ignore it

Your Content

"One must be cringe before they can become based."

For MOST people — not all — you will have to post some cheesy content at the start. I was recently listening to a podcast with Jen Sincero and this is something that holds a lot of people back.

"Oh I don't want to post platitude content."

"List tweets? That's lame, there are too many."

"All I want to do is shitpost..."

Sorry.. not gonna happen. You are the only one that is aware of them being "cheesy."

Don't play the losing fight against human nature.

Put in the necessary reps until you're at a point where you can show a bit more personality.

Why can big YouTuber's post anything they want and still grow? Because people know them and they have social proof. They put in the initial reps.

They didn't start that way. Go look at anyone's account and you will see they all played nice with the algorithm. They got views, engagement, followers, and then slowly started to do whatever they want.

As Jack Butcher put it: "Build distribution, then build whatever you want."

If you want a cheatcode to content you can create, check out my swipe file here and plug your ideas into them as templates.

Focus Areas

Writing 3 quality tweets per day (focused on growth)  
Long list tweets give people more reasons to follow you  
Confident, pain or benefit focused basic content \- speak in absolutes  
Highly actionable content. Step by step how to achieve a desired result, in the form of a list or thread.  
Check out this article on the best content to write (this works extremely well).  
Engaging with 10+ people per day  
Forming mastermind groups and making lifelong friends  
This is arguably the most important step  
Getting your content retweeted by paying for promotions or networking with big people

Under 20,000 Followers

From 1,000 to 20,000 (ish) you will be introducing the authenticity side of your brand. Authority, authenticity, and growth all interconnect... and its not like you avoid any of them along the way — but now you are consciously putting effort into the more "human" side of your brand.

You are doubling down on what has worked for growth. Paying attention to what people respond to, and starting to form your message.

This is important. Stop stressing about your niche or content pillars. Talk about what you want in a way that will result in growth. You will naturally find your talking points. I cannot teach this. It must be done on your own.

Keep posting lists. Test new kinds of tweets. Incorporate your own flare or humor.

At this point, things are getting easy.

Focus Areas:

Consistent, high quality content  
Connecting with higher level players since you have some social capital  
Maintaining relationships with those you've connected with in mastermind groups (keeping friendships and helping each other grow)  
Building out systems for your content creation  
Turning tweets into email topics  
Using TweetHunter to write weeks worth of tweets so you can focus on building and selling offers  
Spending time absorbing information from your "Tribe of Mentors" (big brands you aspire to be like)

Under 50,000 Followers

At this point you have your main talking points. It's time to ideate these and make them yours.

Your job is to start coining names for your ideas or speaking on specific things.

Examples:  
The One Person Business Model (freelancing, coaching, creating)  
Lifestyle Design (productivity, flow)  
A portfolio of small bets (Daniel Vassalo's way of saying "throw shit at a wall and see what sticks")  
Build Once, Sell Twice (Jack Butcher's way of saying build digital products that you can sell infinitely)

Think of this as simplifying concept topics into a memorable "label"

This will only help you grow faster. People will mention you in posts when they talk about your concept.

Next step: start branching out to other platforms in a sustainable way.

You've solidified your message, offer, and what you want to get across.

Podcasts are great for your brand's authenticity pillar. It builds a deeper connection and allows you to be vulnerable.

Consistent newsletters allow you to show authority or entertain your audience.

YouTube is powerful if you want to speak and create captivating videos.

Instagram is just a no brainer because everyone is on there.

You can use this template if you would like \- it will help you break down a long form post (that you can use for blog, email, YouTube script, etc) into tweets, reels, Instagram posts and the rest.

Focus Areas:  
Twitter is on autopilot now  
Start learning the other platforms you are trying to grow on  
Create systems for content creation and make it easy on yourself  
Have one project that you are building out at a time (offer, book, community)

50,000+ (My Current Strategy)

At this point, I'm coasting. I don't have to do much to continue growing. I've gone through my "cheesy" phase and I can start to build real authority.

I plan on playing LONG term games with short term initial payouts.

ITERABLE GAMES: Do the things that make you look back and make you cringe at yourself.

The podcast is starting slow but is picking up momentum.

YouTube is slowly growing without me having to post content for the algorithm.

I am writing and publishing a book. Trying to make it a NYT bestseller so I can tap into top tier personal brand's networks and infinitely scale through their platforms.

The Power Planner 2.0 will be a staple in peoples days.

Kinda like world domination (for good\!) on a micro level.

I hope this post was insightful. If you have any questions pop em in the \#business-strategy or writing-and-idea-generation channel\!

---
