# The Ultimate Twitter Thread Writing Guide

In preparation for our 7 Days of Threads Sprint in the Discord community, here is a thread writing masterclass.

Why should you care about threads?  
They bring in a massive amount of followers. The longer and more in depth they are, the more followers they bring.  
They are great for sales. Just plug your product / lead magnet at the end.  
You can repurpose them into tweets, emails, blog posts, YouTube scripts, and any other content.  
They build authority, trust, and a deeper connection with your audience.  
If you can get people to retweet them, you can grow from 0-1K followers faster than ever.

Threads are just expanded tweets. Keep this in mind when you are deciding the intention of your thread.

I would recommend reading over The Social Matrix to understand the growth, authenticity, and authority pillars.

Is it for growth?  
Tweet your story or a part of your story  
Most threads (no matter growth, authenticity, or authority) will result in growth.

Is it for authenticity?  
Tweet your personal experience or struggles you've overcome  
Document what you are going to do while you are "building in public"

Is it for authority?  
Drop massive value relating to what you teach.  
Give beginners step by step advice.  
Call out your audience and tell them what they are doing wrong.  
IF IT IS FOR AUTHORITY \- Call out your audience in the eyebrow.

Threads, when done right, are a mixture of all 3\. The primary intention of the thread should be focused on growth and authority \- sprinkle in authenticity by writing in your own voice, like you are talking to a friend.

How To Pick A Thread Topic

There are a few types of threads that do very well:  
A numbered list (like a blog) with short or long insights about each point.  
A story of yourself or a client that accomplished something your audience wants to accomplish. (Think transformations)  
Search for multiple variations of an idea you have on Google and make your own spinoff of a blog or YouTube video headline.  
Calling out a problem your target audience and teaching them how to solve it.

This part should be easy. Type parts of your Content Pyramid into Google, YouTube, or just go off the top of your head.

(Your content pyramid is a breakdown of your main topics into sub-topics into content ideas).

DO NOT SLEEP ON THIS METHOD. It has brought previous people in the program hundreds of followers a day. The Google, Medium, or YouTube content is already proven to do well. Take the idea, watch the video, and write about the topic in your own words. "Steal like an artist."

Principles of Thread Writing

Don’t be afraid of writing in-depth content, but make sure that your first impression will leave the reader hungry for more.

Threads are about two things:  
Giving your unique perspective on a particular topic  
Building your expertise and authority on the Twitter space

Threads are like writing a sales letter.

The components are the same:  
Hook \- attention grabbing first line (optional)  
If this is for authority \- call out your audience here.  
"If you are X, Y, Z..."  
Describe the big problem about the topic you are going to discuss. How does it affect your audience? BE SPECIFIC.  
Headline \- mention the big problem you plan to solve and why it needs to be solved.   
Read this blog article on how to write killer blog headlines (these work well for threads)  
Deck \- Introduces the story with curiosity (optional)  
Lead \- AFTER the first tweet in the thread. The lead paints a picture of the problem people are having and hints at a solution.  
Social Proof \- Tell people why they should listen to what you have to say on that topic. (optional)

All are important, but the first tweet is the MOST important tweet of the thread. The first tweet contains the eyebrow, headline, and deck \- but sometimes it just works well with the headline.

If your first tweet sucks, your thread won't perform, so a lot of emphasis on writing your first tweet well (Which should be your eyebrow-headline-deck).

Here are some examples of great threads:

Highly Effective: Hook \+ headline that solves that desire  
https://twitter.com/thealexmarquis/status/1415680070635560966?s=20

Headline \+ Deck  
https://twitter.com/Julian/status/1348001394104537089?s=20

Headline  
https://twitter.com/naval/status/1002103360646823936?s=20

Simple Yet Powerful Headline  
https://twitter.com/PaikCapital/status/1357002717743480834?s=20

Headline  
https://twitter.com/YouActualized/status/1347937301939281922?s=20

Hook \+ Social Proof \+ Mini Number based headline  
https://twitter.com/heyblake/status/1414937660842385411?s=20

Headline  
https://twitter.com/sweatystartup/status/1345855691068764161?s=20

Personal Story With 2x3 Tweet Structure  
https://twitter.com/Psypreneur/status/1356320146349031430?s=20

If you want to see what your favorite accounts have written threads on and study them, type this into the Twitter search bar.

from:thedankoe "thread"

The Rest Of Your Thread

The way you want to structure a thread (or any type of content really) is by having a beginning/middle/end structure to it.  
Beginning \= hook \+ problem   
The hook includes the eyebrow, headline, and deck  
The problem is the lead (and usually takes up 1-2 tweets in length)  
Middle \= key talking points   
Think about how a blog article is structured with subcategories  
End \= closure/lesson learned and call to action   
Wrap up the thread with the lesson you learned or a recap on what the reader learned  
You have their attention \- so ask them to do something \- like buy a product, DM you for your services, download a lead magnet, and ALWAYS ask them to retweet the first tweet, it helps.  
If you have a product, you can offer to give it away free to one retweeter.

🔑 Remember, it's not about content length. It's not about the number of tweets. It's about providing valuable information and making your reader feel something.

An example of a failed thread:  
https://twitter.com/sweatystartup/status/1352366082942775296?s=20

Another one from Nick but the initial tweet is too messy, it loses people's interest.

It doesn't have 1 big idea, it doesn't spark any curiosity, and I don't immediately see a "What's in it for me?" reason for me to continue reading.

🔑 Remember, curiosity \+ benefit (make the reader curious \+ give them a reason the read more) is the key for a thread to bang.

Getting Maximum Exposure

We all know networking is good \- but being able to send a thread to your network to retweet is an INSANE growth hack.

If you haven't already, start making friends in the DMs. DO NOT ask for a retweet if you have never DMd the person before. Make friends first, even if it's a very short conversation.

Once you have a network \- send them the tweet and be authentic:  
"Yo brother just wrote up this thread, would truly appreciate if you gave it an RT. If not, no worries, and if theres anything I can do for you let me know\!"  
If you have a decent following, you can offer to trade retweets (an example of exponential growth and social capital).

Adding Examples of People That Align With Key Points

If you want to guarantee that some tweets get good exposure, tag people that understand whatever topic you are talking about well.

If I write a thread on my fitness transformation and going on walks are a big part of that \- I could tag someone who also is a proponent of going on walks when I mention walks.

If I write a thread on building a Twitter account and mention learning how to write well, I can tag a big writing account and give them some praise.

If I write a thread on X and want to give the readers Y resources, I can tag someone that provides Y resources.

A lot of the time the accounts you tag will retweet the thread as a whole.

If you enjoyed this thread, let me know in the \#business-strategy channel.

If you have any questions, post them there as well\!

For bonus points and an RT, post your thoughts about it on Twitter and tag me.

# The Best Social Media Engagement Group Structure

Whether you are for or against the idea of engagement groups \- they are an extremely good way of:

Leveraging other's network of followers  
Making lifelong connections (Joey and I met in an engagement group, look at us now)  
Strategizing with those at a similar level as you, sharing new tactics you are learning  
Staying active on the timeline and building your tribe (people will start to associate you with those people, and it will build a stronger connection with your audience)

The general problem with engagement groups is that they aren't structured. People send posts at every second of the day... some don't send, and the group ends up dying out.

This is the strategy that I used from 5K to 50K ish followers. It's simple and doesn't require you to share a ton of posts and destroy your feed.

Below I've embedded a video explaining exactly how to structure the group using this excel sheet (click "File \> Make a copy" and then you can edit).

I would HIGHLY recommend posting in the \#business-strategy channel to form a mastermind group with other members of MMHQ. Or you can DM people individually here or on socials based on their follower count being relative to yours.

I hope this helps\! Happy social growth.

P.S. This works for any social media platform. Instead of retweeting, it is sharing. On Instagram it is a story share, on LinkedIn it is sharing the post, etc etc.

# The Best Growth Content For Social Media (and how to create it FAST)

As many of you know, I am a HUGE fan of emulation.

That is \- picking something that works on the funnel level and differentiating yourself on the brand level (mostly personal brands in our case).

Funnel \= content, copy, landing pages, free products, paid products, services, and how you get people to buy. There is somebody in your industry that has already figured it out \- steal from them.

Brand \= why they choose to buy from you. Usually based on authenticity or authority (see: Twitter Matrix).

We will be discussing the "growth" factor that fuels both of these. Your organic content \- free lead generation.

How To Generate Unlimited Viral Content Ideas

The secret: DO WHAT WORKS.

You probably already follow brands that are similar to you. They have done something right somewhere along the way. Your job is to find that content and recreate it under your brand.

Where do you find content ideas?

Most popular YouTube videos from creators in your niche  
Top ranking blog posts found through Google search  
The featured articles on Medium based on your interests  
Top tweets from creators in your niche  
You can type "from:thedankoe min\_faves:500" in the twitter search bar to find tweets of mine that have gotten over 500 likes. You can do this for any creator, just replace the handle after "from:"  
Pinterest, Instagram, TikTok \- I have not figured out how to find the best posts, but if they get high engagement you can take them

How do you use these content ideas?

The content you find will be tried and true (especially the YouTube videos, they work wonders for idea generation).

YouTube videos, podcasts, and articles can be turned into threads. You can also turn ideas from those videos into individual tweets.

The main thing you are looking for here is the headline or video title.

Your job is to take that big idea and turn it into content that falls under your brand.

A headline can be turned into:

Short form content (tweet, insta post, another headline)  
An idea for your own expansion on that idea

The content in a video can be turned into:

List style tweets / social posts (if the original content is structured / numbered)  
Individual tweets from a random "knowledge bomb"  
Threads that are already structured for you

YOU ARE NOT PLAGIARIZING. YOU ARE EMULATING WHAT WORKS. YOU NEED EXPERIENCE, SKILL, AND KNOWLEDGE IN THAT SPECIFIC AREA TO REWRITE IT AS YOUR OWN. I am assuming you all have this and will use this ethically.

This is what everyone does. We all just steal from each other and our buyers are determined by our branding \+ marketing \+ getting in front of their face with the right offer.

There is only so much you can talk about for a specific topic \- so why not talk about the ideas that work?

We all have our own unique biases that will make these unique. This is an art.

The Natural Evolution

The longer you are in the game (through more experience and iteration) the more you will gravitate towards deeper content that SCREAMS \*insert your brand here\*.

When you are just starting out \- you are somewhat forced to create basic content that is proven to work. Nobody knows who you are or what you are about \- you need time, repetition, and an audience for that.

Grow by creating content that is proven to work. Slowly introduce your authentic voice, and make sure to establish authority along the way.

# The Best Products / Services & Niches To Sell To On Twitter

My friends\! I wanted to write this up before I leave for my trip.

I know many of you are beginners in the online business space, so hopefully this will help clear some things up and give you a game plan.

If you haven't already, read this article, The $5K Fast Track, either before or after you read this. It will tell you what to do after you have sufficiently learned a skill stack.

The Best Niches To Sell To On Twitter

Personal brands in general  
Ecommerce stores  
Info product creators  
Coaches / consultants  
AUTHORS  
Agency owners  
Founders / executives  
Busy 9-5ers  
A group of people that have offers but don't understand how to get an sales / leads via Twitter  
The beginner market in any industry (health, wealth, relationships)  
Service businesses (usually a one-man show that has a personal brand)  
Big corporate brands (Wendy's, Gillette, etc)

Twitter is a different space than Instagram or Facebook. You must understand Twitter as a platform to see this.

There aren't pages, maps, etc that are helpful for finding local businesses. So, don't target local businesses, or any business that you would would have difficulty finding on Twitter.

The Best Products / Services To Sell To Those Niches

Sell what is already selling. Run it through the other marketing frameworks in this channel and it will sell better. You are simply taking a piece of the pie.

Services To Sell:

In order to sell these services effectively, you need to get on the phone with somebody in your target niche and understand their client acquisition process. You are going to "patch the holes" in that process and increase their revenue via more product sales or lead generation.

That is for marketing services (email, design, lead gen, etc), not coaching / consulting that falls under the health / relationships vertical. Some coaching can go after the "increase business revenue" angle though.

Twitter account management, growth, and ghostwriting  
To any of the niches above  
Instagram account management, growth, and content creation  
To Twitter creators / personal brands that struggle to be consistent with Instagram (you can take their Twitter content and repurpose it).  
Fitness coaching  
For executives, founders, busy 9-5ers, or any non-business owner that can afford high ticket coaching  
Performance coaching  
To the same niches as fitness coaching  
Email marketing (sequences and broadcasts)  
To eCommerce stores, agency owners, personal brands, coaches  
Funnel creation (for info products, coaching, or both)  
To info product creators and coaches / consultants  
Authors, to sell more books (and possibly consult them on creating a higher ticket offer)  
High ticket sales (being a high ticket closer)  
Anyone with a high ticket offer (coaching, consulting, marketing service) or a high ticket course  
Influencers, creators, freelancers, agency owners  
Content multiplication / repurposing (taking tweets, videos, blogs, or whatever their main form of content is and editing it to post across more platforms)  
Example: taking tweets and making Instagram posts  
Example: taking YouTube videos, writing a blog post out of it, clipping the video for Instagram and TikTok, and then editing the audio for a podcast  
Niches: Any personal brand that already has strong content on any platform

For all of these... run through the Solopreneur Foundations training, the $5K Fast Track, and Your Marketing Strategy in One Sentence (and the articles tagged inside that).

Your job is to quite literally copy somebody that has already figured it out and get good at branding / marketing yourself (check out Personal Brand Mastery w/ Eddy)

This comes heavily into play for products as well.

The Best Products To Sell

Wonder why everyone and their mom has a Twitter growth guide? Because they sell. Well.

So, our first product that sells well is Twitter related.

If you want to sell something Twitter-related and not get memed off the face of the earth, RUN IT THROUGH THE MARKETING POSTS IN HERE.

The Twitter Growth angle is okay \- but you know what would sell more?

The Twitter Lead Multiplier \- that helps creators and coaches build out a Twitter-specific funnel to landing more clients.

In reality it's just a funnel and understanding of how to leverage Twitter for traffic \- but it would be seen as a powerful and authoritative product that would get quality buyers into YOUR funnel.

It would also have much of the same information as a Twitter growth guide.

Selling Your Unique System

I encourage people to create a high ticket offer first (see services to sell from above).

You can start landing clients immediately with this.

Then, once you have results, you can literally just turn your process for getting results into an info product and have all of the marketing done. You already know it will sell.

Even if the system isn't "unique" per se \- that's where marketing comes in. Narrow your target audience and sell to an individual.

Products That Sell

Productivity systems  
Business systems (how you get sales / clients for a specific niche above)  
Make any process in ones life simpler (example: twitter content creation for personal brands \- this is another angle that is better than the traditional "twitter growth")  
Weight loss programs  
Body part specific muscle building programs  
Individual specific muscle building programs (body type)  
Teaching a specific skill (marketing or otherwise)  
ANYTHING \- you just have to be able to market it effectively (yes I'm serious). This takes experience and practice/iteration to understand fully

Pay close attention to what others are doing, especially the accounts you want to be like.

Sign up for their newsletters, buy their products, study their funnels, and see where you would be able to help them (or steal ideas from them).

I hope this article helped\!

# The Simplified Product Launch Guide

Product launches should not be taken lightly. They have the potential to make you a lot of money. There are 2 ways to go about this:

Simply not care and launch (has its benefits)  
Care a lot, prepare, and make a ton of money

The first is fine if you are a new creator with a few followers. It is a good thing to just say "fuck it" and launch your minimum viable product.

You can always turn the product into something else  
You can always use that product as promotional firepower elsewhere  
You can iterate on the product and launch a better version when you have more followers.

The second is clearly the best option \- but I recommend doing it with a minimum of 5,000 followers.

You will have connections that can affiliate and blow up your launch posts  
You can leverage their audiences and your own since they will be over 5,000  
You will ACTUALLY have an audience that you can nurture and season with content before you launch.

Let's dive into the actual phases of launch.

Pre-Requisites

Having gone through previous articles in the Marketing & Ideation channel and have the general marketing strategy for your product locked down.

The product does not have to be complete \- but you should have a general outline of the problem you are solving and how exactly you are solving that problem.

Seasoning & Pre-Hype

The great thing about a personal brand is that you can talk about whatever you want, but as we learned earlier \- when it comes to sales \- we need to get specific and authoritative.

1-2 weeks leading up to your launch you will be posting to start moving readers up the levels of customer awareness.

From unaware of their problem to aware of it and wanting to fix it. When you put your product in front of their phase everything will make sense, and they will buy if done right.

What Do You Post?

Answer the questions from your market research in the form of tweets and threads. Threads are the ultimate authority builder.   
If you can write 2-3 threads on the subject before you launch, that's amazing (these threads can be turned into emails, videos, articles, and multiple tweets.)  
You can turn sections from your product into threads fairly easily. Don't be afraid to give away too much value. Free value is forgotten and isn't acted on.  
Tell VS Show   
Tell people what to do rather than showing them.  
Tell example: Do market research, create a product, and sell it on Twitter  
Show example: Actually show them your market research process, how you create a product, and how you promote it on Twitter  
Have at least one tweet a day related to your product.  
Have an occasional post (2-3 times a week) letting them know that you will be launching a product that solves X problems for X audience.

Preparation For Massive Exposure

By now there should be at least 5-10 people that you can reach out to and let them know that you are preparing to launch a product. Offer to pay them for exposure if you want, but most of them will help out for free if they believe in you and your product.

If you do not have 5-10 people that can help bring you more exposure (and possibly affiliate for your launch) then you need to start now.

Assets You Should Prepare

Multiple launch emails hitting different levels of customer awareness  
Multiple affiliate launch emails to leverage their email lists  
Multiple promotional tweets (test them all and double down on the copy / angles that bring the most sales)  
Multiple affiliate launch tweets  
1-3 launch threads (take information from the product and turn it into a thread, remember: tell don't show)  
General communication with affiliates and others that are just helping support the launch. Consider putting them into a TG group together.

Take the time to plan this out to the best of your ability. Launches are where the most money is made and can build a LOT of authority for yourself when done organically.

This will be a point in your entrepreneurial career where you will gain many followers (because they are interested in what you are creating), and make a ton of cash.

Launch Phases

There are multiple launch phases \- all of them have the potential to make a lot of money. Let's run through them.

Use this Product Launch Map below to plan out your launch phases and keep things organized.

Product Launch Map (Duplicate to edit)

Presale

Presale is optional.

It is also a great way to make sure your product gets done.  
This is an example of the term I like to throw around, "tactical stress."

If you are procrastinating in creating your product and deciding on a launch date \- start a presale.

This will force you to set a launch date and stone and get your minimum viable product out before then.

This will also let you know what areas need improvement based on the sales you get.

(Presales won't get a ton of sales, but they can get quite a few.)

Crucial Presale Points

Start your price low   
Depending on your confidence in the launch, start at $17 \- $47  
This is heavily dependent on the actual offer and can go up to $497  
As you promote, continuously mention the launch date and that the price will increase (scarcity).  
Shamelessly promote more and more \- up to 2 times a day \- as you near launch date.

Launch Week

Launch week is simple.

PROMOTE. PROMOTE. PROMOTE.

Attack from all angles you can. Write different tweets handling different objections and use as much social proof as humanly possible.

Every time you put out a tweet, ask your network to engage with it. They don't have to RT, just ask them to like and reply to it for social proof reasons.

Promote 1-2 times a day for the entire week. Make sure everyone in your audience knows that you launched a product.

It is also crucial to remind affiliates to promote. Either have them in a Telegram group or DM them individually and ask them if they need anything for their promotions.

Leverage their audience as much as you can.

Post Launch

If you plan to have this as a core offer in your value ladder \- it doesn't stop there.

If this is a micro product that you don't really care about \- you can skip to the second part of this section where we talk about repurposing the information.

Extending The Lifetime of Your Product

After launch, your job is to get creative with promotions to keep sales coming in steadily.

Having guest appearances to teach a subject (to leverage their audience and broaden who your product targets)  
Adding on a bonus of your own or another product  
Offering to pay for products you affiliate for (this works well for memberships because you get MRR)  
Building out a follow-up product to sell to buyers.  
Slowly increase the price by $10-$20 at a time when it feels right. This is usually every month or so but allows you to keep scarcity high.

Repurposing Dead Products

Eventually your product will lose the hype, and that's okay, here's what you can do:

Launch another product, wait until it "dies" and then bundle them together for a cheaper price.  
Use the dead product as a bonus for a new one.  
Using them as incentives for video testimonials.  
Using them as a very cheap tripwire so you can get more "buyers" and put them into buyers email sequences (segmentation.

This article is crucial \- you should plan this launch out carefully and strategize with your network. If you have any questions about this leave it in the \#business-strategy channel.

---

# The Social Matrix For Authoritative Audience Growth

There are 3 crucial aspects of growing an audience:

Authority  
Growth (obviously)  
Authenticity

If one of these falls, you become a commodity. We do NOT want this. We want our account to be an asset.

You need balanced mixture of this content to make it work.

60% growth  
20% authenticity  
20% authority

If you tweet 5 times a day (recommended) you would have:

3 growth tweets  
1 authenticity tweet  
1 authority tweet

This creates leverage. What does this mean?

It means nobody can replace you. You become your own niche. Your expertise \+ unreplicable experiences \+ attention \= leverage.

You eliminate all competition and gain loyal followers (on Twitter that is).

Growth

There are many things that attribute to growth (authority and authenticity HELP), but you need content to be retweetable. How do you make content retweetable?

Tweet about topics that are already doing well  
Turn your personal experiences into relatable insights  
Simple advice based on your content pillars. Write at a 5th grade level.  
General health, wealth, and relationship advice.

The easiest way to understand what I'm saying is by understanding the format of viral blog posts. Tweets are just mini blog posts.

Headlines \= short tweets, list tweets (9 signs a person is really happy with their life), and you can turn each point into tweets.

Retweetable content leads to growth and intertwines with authority \- the more followers and engagement you get, the more people respect you. Weird, but true.

Growth tweets will get the most engagement. Don't get discouraged if the others don't get much engagement.

Authenticity

Authenticity shows people that you are a human. You display this by:

Tweeting about your losses and how you plan to overcome them (don't pity post, tell them what you are doing to be better).  
Giving advice contrary to what people are used to in your niche.  
Documentation: show people what you are doing in real life (photos and videos encouraged but optional)   
What are you working on? What does your lifestyle look like? What did you eat? What does your niche audience do that you also do?  
Post about your likes and interests.   
What kind of music do you listen to? How can you display your personality?

Tweet once a day for authenticity to help nurture the followers you gained with growth.

Authority

Authority tweets help prove your expertise \- these start warming people up for sales.

You can either tweet direct concepts from your current products or other actionable information to your target audience.

These should be very specific meaning you should call out who you are targeting, their pain points, and (optional) how to fix them.

Example: Entrepreneurs are good at making money, but at a sacrifice to their health. Your quality of work suffers and revenue is limited in growth. Health is wealth.  
Step by step posts to solving this pain point work as well (see: blog post style tweets)  
SOCIAL PROOF: This does not necessarily mean posting a screenshot of a review. This means telling a story of where they were before and what they accomplished working with you.   
Having a screenshot of a review will make it seem promotional and get less engagement.  
Telling a story will get a ton of engagement because it inspires people. They will be in the comments congratulating them.  
Then, all you have to do is plug a link or ask them to DM you.  
(Remember to mention your specific target audience here.)

Authority tweets are what will make you the most sales. Promote once a day \- whether its a free or paid product/service.

---
